Parallels in Dualism: Mu'tazila and Magians
Maturidi enumerates parallels between Mu'tazila and Magians on power and creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key parallels Maturidi draws between the Mu'tazila and the Magians regarding the creation of actions and the separation of divine power.

Core Idea
Both Mu'tazila and Magians split God's power, creating a subtle dualism.

Maturidi continues his critique of the Mu'tazila by comparing them to the Magians. This passage lists several specific parallels in how both groups divide the creative power between God and another agent. Pay close attention to how each parallel mirrors the other, and notice the common thread of denying God's full sovereignty over all events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the structure: each parallel is introduced with 'and likewise' or similar.
The passage uses repetitive phrasing to emphasize the comparison.
2
Identify each parallel
List out each distinct point of comparison: (1) attribution of the world's events to bodies, (2) power to create evil, (3) separation of domains of power.
The third parallel includes a difference: Mu'tazila extend this to all living beings, Magians limit it to Iblis.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: why does Maturidi consider this a valid critique? What does it say about the Mu'tazila's view of God's power?
The core problem is that both groups effectively deny God's exclusive creative power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المعتزلة تجعل العالم بالله وبالأجسام من غير أن كان ذلك من الله، من الاجتماع والتفرق والحركة والسكون وجميع المتولدات عن الخلق مفصولا أو بائنا، وكذلك جميع العالم بل المجوس ينسبون كثيرا من الجواهر إلى إبليس، لا تقدر المعتزلة على نسبة شيء ذلك إلى الله فى الحقيقة، والمجوس يثبتون لإبليس القدرة على خلق الشر بالله وينفونها عن الله، وكذلك قول المعتزلة فى قدرة أفعال الخلق، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والمجوس لا تجعل لإبليس على شي مما لله من العالم قدرة، ولا لله على شيء مما للخلق لإبليس، وكذلك أمر المعتزلة، لكنهم جعلوا لجميع الأحياء ذلك، والمجوس لإبليس خاصة . والمجوس لا تجعل الله إرادة ولا سلطانا فيما ليس فيه أمر، وكذلك المعتزلة . والمعنى الذي دعا المجوس إلى القول باثنين ما استقبحوا من إضافة خلق الشر وفساد الأشياء إلى الله، وكذلك المعتزلة . ولو عرفوا حق معرفة الربوبية أنه فى وضع كل شيء موضعه، وأنه المتعالى عن أن يكون فعله لنفع له أو الخير يكتسب لنفسه لعلموا أن الوصف بخلق الكل على ما عليه وصف القدرة والجلال، والقول به قول بتمام الملك والكبرياء، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعبارة أخرى مما تبين أن المعتزلة أحق من يتعالى بالا أنطق الله به ألسن الخلق بالنسبة إليهم صغارهم وكبارهم من علم ما تحت الاسم أو جهله مثبت أن ذلك صار لهم لقبا لا من حيث صنع للبشر فيه، ولكن بفضل
Then the Muʿtazila make the world [come to be] by God and by bodies, without that being from God — from conjunction and separation, motion and rest, and all the generated acts (mutawallidāt) of creatures, whether separated or distinct. And likewise [they attribute] the entire world. Rather, the Magians attribute many substances to Iblīs. The Muʿtazila are not able to attribute anything of that to God in reality. And the Magians affirm for Iblīs the power to create evil under God, and they deny it to God. And likewise is the statement of the Muʿtazila regarding the power over the acts of creatures. And there is no power except with God. The Magians do not affirm for Iblīs any power over anything of the world that belongs to God, nor for God any power over anything that belongs to Iblīs among the creatures. And likewise is the case of the Muʿtazila, except that they made that for all living beings, while the Magians [made it] for Iblīs specifically. The Magians do not affirm for God any will or authority in what is not His affair, and likewise the Muʿtazila. The meaning that led the Magians to the statement of two [principles] is that they deemed it repugnant to attribute the creation of evil and the corruption of things to God, and likewise the Muʿtazila. If they had known the true knowledge of lordship — that it consists in placing everything in its proper place, and that He is exalted above His act being for His own benefit or for acquiring good for Himself — they would have known that describing [Him] as creating all things as they are is a description of power and majesty, and to say so is to affirm complete sovereignty and grandeur. And there is no power except with God. Another expression which makes evident that the Muʿtazila are more deserving to be exalted—God has made the tongues of creatures speak concerning them, small and great, whether one knows the meaning of the name or is ignorant of it, confirming that this became a label for them, not from any human action in it, but by virtue of [God's] favor... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 914

Commentary
This passage continues the comparison between the Muʿtazila and the Magians, listing several specific parallels. First, the Muʿtazila attribute the world's caused phenomena (like motion, rest, generated actions) to both God and bodies (i.e., human agents), thereby removing those events from God's direct creation. Similarly, the Magians attribute many substances to Iblīs. Second, the Magians affirm that Iblīs has the power to create evil under God and deny that power to God; the Muʿtazila similarly affirm that humans have power over their actions, thereby denying God's exclusive power. Third, the Magians limit power: Iblīs has no power over what belongs to God, and God has no power over what belongs to Iblīs. The Muʿtazila do the same, but they extend that power to all living beings (humans), whereas the Magians restrict it to Iblīs. Fourth, the Magians deny God's will and authority in matters outside His immediate concern (i.e., evil), and the Muʿtazila also deny God's will in human acts. Finally, Maturidi identifies the underlying motive: both groups are repulsed by attributing evil and corruption to God, so they resort to dualism. He then refutes this by explaining that true lordship means placing everything in its proper place; God is exalted above doing things for His own benefit. If they understood this, they would see that attributing all creation to God is a statement of power and majesty, not a defect. The passage ends with a remark about how the label Qadariyya has become attached to the Muʿtazila by divine decree, though the text is incomplete.

Key Terms
المتولدات
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that attributing some acts to humans is not dualism.
Correction: Maturidi shows it parallels the Magian dualism of two creators, even if one is a creature.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, how do the Mu'tazila differ from the Magians in the third parallel?
A) Mu'tazila limit the separate domain to Iblis
B) Mu'tazila extend the separate domain to all living beings
C) Mu'tazila deny power to any creature
D) Mu'tazila affirm God's power over all

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses three parallels to expose that the Mu'tazila, like the Magians, effectively divide creative power between God and creatures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life do you functionally believe that your own power is separate from Allah's, even as you profess tawhid? Which parallel from this passage convicts you most?
?
Have you ever, even subtly, thought that some good or evil in your life comes from sources other than Allah? How does Maturidi's comparison with the Magians expose that your heart might share their dualism?
?
Maturidi says the Mu'tazila cannot attribute anything to God in reality. Is there any part of your worldview that, if honestly examined, would show you also reserve a domain for yourself where Allah is not the sole creator and controller? What concrete steps can you take today to hand that domain back to Him?

The Real Motive and Refutation
Maturidi reveals the shared motive and refutes it with correct understanding of lordship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi says the Mu'tazila and Magians share a common motivation—repugnance to attributing evil to God—and how he refutes that position by explaining true lordship.

Core Idea
True lordship means placing everything, even evil, in its proper place.

Having established the structural parallels, Maturidi now digs deeper to uncover the shared psychological motive: both groups find it repugnant to attribute the creation of evil to God. He then offers a profound refutation rooted in the correct understanding of divine lordship. This lesson explores that motivation and Maturidi's corrective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the clear rhetorical shift: 'The meaning that led the Magians...' introduces the motive, then 'If they had known...' begins the refutation.
2
Identify the common motive
Underline the sentence: 'they deemed it repugnant to attribute the creation of evil and the corruption of things to God.' This is the core motivation.
Both groups felt that attributing evil to God would be improper, so they posited separate creators.
3
Analyze the refutation
Maturidi argues that true lordship (rububiyya) means putting everything in its proper place and is beyond benefit. Therefore, describing God as creator of all is a description of majesty, not defect.
Note the contrast: evil is not a defect in God's act but part of His sovereign placement.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with a remark about the label 'Qadariyya'. Consider how this fits Maturidi's argument that the Mu'tazila are more deserving of that label by divine decree.
The text is incomplete, but the thrust is clear: the label is a mark of divine disfavor.

Commentary
This passage continues the comparison between the Muʿtazila and the Magians, listing several specific parallels. First, the Muʿtazila attribute the world's caused phenomena (like motion, rest, generated actions) to both God and bodies (i.e., human agents), thereby removing those events from God's direct creation. Similarly, the Magians attribute many substances to Iblīs. Second, the Magians affirm that Iblīs has the power to create evil under God and deny that power to God; the Muʿtazila similarly affirm that humans have power over their actions, thereby denying God's exclusive power. Third, the Magians limit power: Iblīs has no power over what belongs to God, and God has no power over what belongs to Iblīs. The Muʿtazila do the same, but they extend that power to all living beings (humans), whereas the Magians restrict it to Iblīs. Fourth, the Magians deny God's will and authority in matters outside His immediate concern (i.e., evil), and the Muʿtazila also deny God's will in human acts. Finally, Maturidi identifies the underlying motive: both groups are repulsed by attributing evil and corruption to God, so they resort to dualism. He then refutes this by explaining that true lordship means placing everything in its proper place; God is exalted above doing things for His own benefit. If they understood this, they would see that attributing all creation to God is a statement of power and majesty, not a defect. The passage ends with a remark about how the label Qadariyya has become attached to the Muʿtazila by divine decree, though the text is incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributing evil to God makes Him imperfect or responsible for sin.
Correction: Maturidi explains that God's act of creating evil is not for His benefit but placing it properly as part of His sovereignty, so it is not a defect.

Checkpoint
What specific aspect of lordship does Maturidi say the Magians and Mu'tazila failed to understand?
A) That God is merciful
B) That lordship means placing everything in its proper place
C) That evil is an illusion
D) That God does not create evil

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes dualistic tendencies by showing that true lordship involves placing all things, including evil, appropriately, and that attributing all creation to God magnifies His sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there an area of your life where you find yourself unwilling to attribute to God's will—some evil or difficulty that you think should not be from Him? How does Maturidi's understanding of lordship challenge you to see that as part of His majesty?
?
When you face corruption in the world, do you secretly wish to believe that God is not fully in control, to protect your image of Him? How does this passage call you to a higher view of His sovereignty?
?
Have you ever judged God's actions by your own sense of what is appropriate, without recognizing that His lordship means placing everything—even what you find repugnant—in its proper place? What would it mean for you to submit to that truth today?

Sects and Disagreements
advanced
10 min
Mu'tazila and Magians on Evil: A Shared Error
Maturidi compares Mu'tazila and Magians on will and creation of evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi equates the Mu'tazila and Magians in their aversion to attributing the creation of evil to God, and how this stems from an incomplete understanding of divine lordship.

Core Idea
Both Mu'tazila and Magians reject God's direct creation of evil due to flawed theology.

This passage from Imam Maturidi draws a striking parallel between the Mu'tazila (a rationalist Islamic sect) and the Magians (Zoroastrians). Despite their apparent differences, Maturidi argues that both groups share the same fundamental error: they find it morally objectionable to attribute the creation of evil to God. By examining their positions, we uncover the importance of affirming God's absolute power and wisdom in all things.

Guided Path
1
Understand the common ground
Read the passage and note how Maturidi says both groups differ only in name (will vs. thought) but are actually the same in reality. Both are condemned.
The passage begins by stating the Mu'tazila call it 'will' and Magians 'thought' but it is one.
2
Identify the contradiction
Notice how both groups assign power to create evil to someone other than God: the Mu'tazila to all living beings, the Magians to Iblis. Yet they still claim God is the creator of the world.
Maturidi points out the inconsistency: they deny God's power over evil but affirm it over good.
3
Recognize the shared motivation
Maturidi explicitly states that the reason the Magians became dualists is because they deemed it reprehensible to attribute evil to God, and the Mu'tazila do the same.
This is the core of the critique: both are driven by moral sensibilities, not true knowledge of God.
4
Grasp the true solution
Maturidi explains that if they knew real lordship—that God places everything properly and is above acting for benefit—they would see that creating all things, including evil, is a sign of power and majesty.
The antidote is to understand that God's actions are not for personal gain but are perfect in wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإرادة من غير أن كان من الله بحدوثها إرادة أو اختيار منه إليها معنى سوى أن كانت ، فكان بها جميع العالم ؛ إذ من قولهم : إن العالم فعل الله ، وإنه كان باختيار ، وإن الاختيار إرادة كقوله : فَعَالُ لِمَا يُرِيدُ. قسمت المعتزلة تلك الحادثة إرادة ، والمجوس فكرة ، وهى واحدة ، بينهما اختلاف في الاسم لا الحقيقة. ثم جعلت المجوس بها يصف العالم ، والمعتزلة كل العالم ، فيكونان في الحاصل تحت قول ذميم، والمعتزلة زائدة . ثم المعتزلة تجعل العالم بالله وبالأجسام من غير أن كان ذلك من الله ، من الاجتماع والتفرق والحركة والسكون وجميع المتولدات عن الخلق مفصولا أو بائنا ، وكذلك جميع العالم العالم بل المجوس ينسبون كثيرا من الجواهر إلى إبليس ، لا تقدر المعتزلة على نسبة شيء ذلك إلى الله فى الحقيقة ، والمجوس يثبتون لإبليس القدرة على خلق الشر بالله وينفونها عن الله ، وكذلك قول المعتزلة فى قدرة أفعال الخلق ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والمجوس لا تجعل لإبليس على شي مما لله من العالم قدرة ، ولا لله على شيء مما للخلق" لإبليس ، وكذلك أمر المعتزلة ، لكنهم جعلوا لجميع الأحياء ذلك ، والمجوس لإبليس خاصة . والمجوس / لا تجعل الله إرادة ولا سلطانا فيما ليس فيه مما عند المجوس من الخير والشر ، أمر ، وكذلك المعتزلة . والمعنى الذي دعا المجوس إلى القول باثنين ما استقبحوا من إضافة خلق الشر وفساد الأشياء إلى الله ، وكذلك المعتزلة . ولو عرفوا حق معرفة الربوبية أنه فى وضع كل شيء موضعه ، وأنه المتعالى عن أن يكون فعله لنفع له أو الخير يكتسب لنفسه لعلموا أن الوصف بخلق الكل على ما عليه وصف القدرة والجلال ، والقول به قول بتمام الملك والكبرياء ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعبارة أخرى مما تبين أن المعتزلة أحق من يتعالى بالا.
The will from other than that it was from God by its occurrence as will or choice from Him to it is a meaning other than that it was, so by it the whole world came to be; since from their statement: that the world is the act of God, and that it was by choice, and that choice is will like His saying: 'Doer of what He wills'. The Mu'tazila divided that occurrence as will, and the Magians as thought, and it is one, between them a difference in name not in reality. Then the Magians made by it describe the world, and the Mu'tazila the whole world, so both are under a blameworthy statement, and the Mu'tazila are excessive. Then the Mu'tazila make the world by God and by bodies from other than that that was from God, from union and separation, movement and stillness, and all generated things from creation, separated or distinct, and likewise the whole world, nay the Magians attribute many substances to Iblis; the Mu'tazila cannot attribute anything of that to God in reality, and the Magians affirm for Iblis the power to create evil by God and deny it from God, and likewise the statement of the Mu'tazila concerning the power of acts of creation, and there is no power except by God. And the Magians do not make for Iblis any power over anything of what belongs to God from the world, nor for God over anything of what belongs to creation from Iblis, and likewise the affair of the Mu'tazila, but they made that for all living beings, and the Magians for Iblis specifically. And the Magians do not make for God will nor authority over what is not in it from what is with the Magians of good and evil, an affair, and likewise the Mu'tazila. And the meaning that called the Magians to say two (gods) is what they deemed reprehensible from attributing the creation of evil and corruption of things to God, and likewise the Mu'tazila. And if they knew the true knowledge of lordship, that He is in placing everything in its place, and that He is exalted above that His act be for benefit to Him or good acquired for Himself, they would know that the description by creating all as it is is a description of power and majesty, and the statement with it is a statement of complete sovereignty and grandeur, and there is no power except by God. And another expression showing that the Mu'tazila are more worthy of being exalted above.
Source pages p. 914

Commentary
This passage compares the doctrines of the Mu'tazila and the Magians (Zoroastrians) regarding the will and the creation of evil. Maturidi begins by stating that the will (al-irāda) from God is a meaning (maʿnā) by which the whole world came to be, citing the Quranic verse 'Doer of what He wills' (Hud 11:107, al-Buruj 85:16). Then he notes that the Mu'tazila call that occurrence 'will' while the Magians call it 'thought' (fikra), but it is one and the same, differing only in name not reality. Both groups are condemned. The Mu'tazila are worse because they attribute all acts of the world, including those of bodies, to God but then separate generated actions from His direct act. Magians attribute many substances to Iblis (Satan). Maturidi points out contradictions: Magians give Iblis power to create evil but deny it from God, while Mu'tazila give that power to living beings. Both groups share the same motivation: they find it morally objectionable to attribute the creation of evil and corruption to God. If they truly understood God's lordship—that He places everything properly and is exalted above acting for benefit or acquiring good—they would see that creating all things, including evil, is consistent with His power and majesty. The passage ends by stating that the Mu'tazila are even more worthy of being 'exalted above' (yataʿālā) in the sense of being criticized, though the phrase is ambiguous.

Key Terms
الإرادة
الاختيار
المعتزلة
المجوس
خلق الشر
إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Maturidi is defending the idea that God creates evil as an evil act, but he is actually affirming that all creation, including evil, is good in terms of divine wisdom and sovereignty.
Correction: Maturidi does not say evil is good; he says that God's creating evil is a sign of His power and majesty, and that God places everything in its proper place according to His wisdom.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the main similarity between the Mu'tazila and the Magians in this passage?
A) They both deny the existence of Iblis.
B) They both deem it reprehensible to attribute the creation of evil to God.
C) They both affirm that God creates all things directly.
D) They both use the same terminology for will.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi critiques both the Mu'tazila and Magians for allowing their moral aversion to evil to shape their theology, whereas true knowledge of God's lordship requires affirming His absolute power over all things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt uncomfortable attributing something bad in your life to Allah's decree? How does this lesson challenge your instinct to distance Him from evil?
?
In what areas of your life do you find yourself acting like the Mu'tazila or Magians—preferring to explain suffering by human free will or external forces rather than submitting to Allah's absolute sovereignty? Will you repent from this and train your heart to say 'Allah has willed it all' even when it's hard?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's creation of all things—good and evil—is a manifestation of His majesty and perfection, how would your reaction to calamities change starting today? Write down one concrete decision you will make in response.

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
4 min
The Divine Origin of the Name 'Mu'tazila'
Maturidi asserts the divine origin of the name 'Mu'tazila' and its purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Maturidi argues the name 'Mu'tazila' was divinely ordained, not coined by humans, and served to warn the People of the Book.

Core Idea
The name 'Mu'tazila' comes from God, not from human invention.

This lesson presents Maturidi's claim that the name 'Mu'tazila' is not a human label but a divine designation. According to him, God made people call them by this name so that the Jews and Christians would recognize them and avoid mixing with them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Maturidi begins with a strong assertion about the origin of the name.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the claim
Find Maturidi's statement that the name became a nickname (لقب) not from human making but by God's grace (بفضل الله).
This is the core claim.
3
Understand the purpose
The purpose is for 'ahl al-dhimma' (People of the Book) to know them and beware of mixing with them. What does this imply about the Mu'tazila?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنطق الله به ألسن الخلق بالنسبة إليهم صغارهم وكبارهم من علم ما تحت الاسم أو جهله مثبت أن ذلك صار لهم لقبا لا من حيث صنع للبشر فيه ، ولكن بفضل الله ، ليعلم به أهل الذمة في الدين ، فيحذر مخالطتهم . ولهم في ذلك علمان ظاهران : أحدهما في لون كل منهم . كل منهم الصفرة الباردة التي تستقبحها الأبصار ، إذا قوبل ذلك بوجوه المجوس لوجدوا سواء . والثاني تخلفهم عن جماعات المجوس وإنكار عامتهم دار الإسلام أن تكون دارهم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ولتحقيق هذا الاسم لهم أيضا وجهان : إن كل ذى دين ومذهب نسب إلى المعنى الذى ادعاه لنفسه بحق الإسلام واليهودية والنصرانية ونحو هذا ، وكذلك المعتزلة يرون قدر أفعالهم لأنفسهم ، وغيرهم يرون ذلك منه ، فحال أن يشتهر به من رآه لغيره ، ويزال عمن يدعى حقيقته لنفسه ، وبمثله جاء عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في شرط الإيمان بالقدر خيره وشره من الله . والوجه الآخر الأمر المعروف الذى لم ير معتزليا سلم عما يزيل عنه اسم الإيمان والتحلى بحلية الإسلام من ارتكاب الكبائر بالشهوات مما يبين استخفافهم بدين الله واختيارهم الخروج منه بأدنى شهوة أعطوها لأنفسهم ، فهم أحق من ينسب إلى غير دين الله ، إذ هذا شأنهم في دينهم الذي هو عندهم دين الله ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم ذكر الكعبي أن ذلك من عادة العرب تلقيب من يلهج بشيء فيكثر ذكره في غير موضعه حتى يجاوز الحد فيه ونسبة ذلك إليه ، وهم يفعلون ذلك حتى قالوا في كل فاحشة وأمر ذميم هذا قدر الله. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : أخطأ فى هذا القدر من الدعوى من أوجه : أحدها ما حكى عن العرب ، والثانى ما حكى عنهم ، هم لا يقولون ذلك وإن كان يقوله.
God made the tongues of creation speak concerning them, their small and their great, those who know what the name contains or are ignorant, affirming that that became a nickname for them, not from where a human made in it, but by God's grace, so that the people of dhimma in religion may know by it, so they may beware of mixing with them. And they have in that two apparent signs: one of them in the color of each of them. Each of them has the cold paleness that eyes consider ugly, if that is compared to the faces of the Magians, they would find them equal. And the second is their staying away from the congregations of the Magians and the denial of their general population of the abode of Islam that it be their abode, and there is no power except by God. And for the verification of this name for them there are also two aspects: every possessor of a religion and sect is attributed to the meaning that he claimed for himself by right of Islam, Judaism, Christianity and the like, and likewise the Mu'tazila see the extent of their acts for themselves, and others see that from him, so it happens that one is famous by it from one who sees it for another, and removed from one who claims its reality for himself, and similar to that came from the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, concerning the condition of belief in destiny, its good and its evil, from God. And the other aspect is the well-known matter that no Mu'tazilite was seen safe from what removes from him the name of faith and adornment with the ornament of Islam, from committing major sins by desires, showing their contempt for the religion of God and their choice to leave it for the least desire they granted themselves, so they are more worthy to be attributed to other than the religion of God, since this is their state in their religion which for them is the religion of God, and there is no power except by God. Then al-Ka'bi mentioned that that is from the custom of the Arabs to nickname one who persists in something and mentions it frequently in other than its place until he exceeds the limit in it, and to attribute that to him, and they do that until they said about every immoral act and blameworthy matter: 'This is the decree of God.' The shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: He erred in this amount of claim in several aspects: one of them is what he narrated about the Arabs, and the second is what he narrated about them; they do not say that, even if he says it.
Source pages p. 915

Commentary
This passage explains the origin of the name 'Mu'tazila' and refutes a claim by al-Ka'bi. Maturidi begins by stating that God caused people to speak of the Mu'tazila by a certain name, which became a nickname for them, not by human invention but by divine grace, so that the People of the Book (ahl al-dhimma) may recognize them and avoid mixing with them. He mentions two visible signs (ʿilmān ẓāhirān) of the Mu'tazila: first, their pale complexion (ṣufra bārida) that is considered ugly, and when compared to Magians they look alike; second, their withdrawal from Magian congregations and their denial that the abode of Islam (dār al-islām) is their abode. Then he gives two aspects (wajhān) to verify the name: first, that every religious group is named by the meaning they claim for themselves (e.g., Muslims, Jews, Christians), and similarly the Mu'tazila see their own acts as coming from themselves, while others see them as coming from God, so the name sticks to those who hold that opinion and is removed from those who claim it falsely; this is supported by a hadith about belief in destiny. The second aspect is that no Mu'tazilite is seen safe from committing major sins (kabāʾir) due to desires, showing their contempt for religion, so they are more deserving to be attributed to a religion other than Islam. Finally, Maturidi reports that al-Ka'bi claimed that the name comes from the Arab custom of nicknaming someone who persists in mentioning something excessively, like saying 'this is the decree of God' about every evil act. The shaykh (Maturidi) refutes this, saying al-Ka'bi erred in two ways: what he narrated about the Arabs is false, and they do not say such things even if he says them.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الاسم
اللقب
أهل الذمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the primary purpose of the name 'Mu'tazila'?
A) To honor the Mu'tazila.
B) To warn the People of the Book against mixing with them.
C) To follow Arab custom.
D) To confuse the masses.

Key Takeaway
The name 'Mu'tazila' was divinely ordained to warn the People of the Book against mixing with them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the labels you use for others—whether Muslim or non-Muslim—carry divine weight, or do you treat them as mere human conventions? How does your daily speech reflect that belief?
?
If God Himself chose a name for a group of people for a specific purpose, how does that challenge your tendency to dismiss or mock names and titles?
?
The passage says the name was given so that ahl al-dhimma would 'beware of mixing' with this group. Have you ever considered that the way you identify yourself or others might be a divine warning against harmful associations? Are you careful about who you mix with?

Two Visible Signs of the Mu'tazila
Maturidi enumerates two visible signs of the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two physical and social signs Maturidi attributes to the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Maturidi points to pale skin and withdrawal from Magian gatherings as marks of the Mu'tazila.

Maturidi provides two observable signs that distinguish the Mu'tazila: their pale complexion resembling Magians, and their refusal to join Magian congregations. These signs, he claims, make them identifiable and show their separation from Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the phrase 'علمان ظاهران' (two apparent signs).
2
Identify the first sign
The first sign is in color: each Mu'tazilite has a cold paleness (الصفرة الباردة) that is considered ugly, and it is identical to the faces of Magians.
Compare with Magians.
3
Identify the second sign
The second sign is their staying away from Magian congregations and their denial that the abode of Islam (دار الإسلام) is their abode.
4
Analyze the purpose
Think about why Maturidi mentions these signs. What do they indicate about the Mu'tazila's relationship to Islam and other religions?
They are associated with Magians and reject Islamic abode.

?

?

?
If someone observed your behavior at gatherings, would they see you as belonging to the abode of Islam or leaning toward the ways of those who oppose it? How can you ensure your presence among Muslims is a sign of your commitment, not your withdrawal?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
Two Verification Aspects for the Name 'Mu'tazila'
Maturidi provides two rational verification aspects for the name 'Mu'tazila'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two rational aspects Maturidi uses to justify the name 'Mu'tazila'.

Core Idea
The name 'Mu'tazila' sticks because they attribute acts to themselves, and they commit major sins.

After giving visible signs, Maturidi presents two reasoned arguments for why the name 'Mu'tazila' is fitting. The first relates to their belief that their actions come from themselves, not God, and the second points to their persistent commission of major sins. These, he argues, make them deserving of a name that separates them from Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to the phrase 'وجهان' (two aspects).
2
Identify the first aspect
The first aspect: every religious group is named by the meaning they claim. The Mu'tazila see their actions as their own (قدر أفعالهم لأنفسهم), unlike others who see them from God. So the name designates those who hold this view.
A hadith about belief in destiny is referenced.
3
Identify the second aspect
The second aspect: it is well-known that Mu'tazilites commit major sins (كبائر) due to desires, showing contempt for religion, so they are more worthy to be attributed to other than the religion of God.
This is a moral argument.
4
Reflect on the argument
Consider how these two aspects together justify the name 'Mu'tazila' as those who 'separate' or 'withdraw' from mainstream Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Refuting al-Ka'bi's Claim on the Name's Origin
Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's alternative etymology for the name 'Mu'tazila'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of al-Ka'bi's claim that the name 'Mu'tazila' originates from Arab custom.

Core Idea
Maturidi rejects al-Ka'bi's explanation as erroneous and factually wrong.

A certain al-Ka'bi argued that the name 'Mu'tazila' came from the Arab practice of nicknaming someone who persistently mentions something, like saying 'this is the decree of God' for evil acts. Maturidi refutes this on two counts: the claim about Arab custom is false, and the Arabs do not actually say such things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the transition 'ثم ذكر الكعبي'.
2
Understand al-Ka'bi's claim
Al-Ka'bi says the name comes from the Arab custom of nicknaming someone who obsessively repeats a phrase, such as saying 'this is God's decree' for every evil act.
This is an alternative etymology.
3
Identify Maturidi's refutation
Maturidi says al-Ka'bi erred in two aspects: his narration about Arab custom is false, and his narration that Arabs say such things is false.
The refutation is concise.
4
Reflect on the refutation
Consider why Maturidi considers this refutation important. What does it indicate about the name's significance?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنطق الله به ألسن الخلق بالنسبة إليهم صغارهم وكبارهم من علم ما تحت الاسم أو جهله مثبت أن ذلك صار لهم لقبا لا من حيث صنع للبشر فيه ، ولكن بفضل الله ، ليعلم به أهل الذمة في الدين ، فيحذر مخالطتهم . ولهم في ذلك علمان ظاهران : أحدهما في لون كل منهم . كل منهم الصفرة الباردة التي تستقبحها الأبصار ، إذا قوبل ذلك بوجوه المجوس لوجدوا سواء . والثاني تخلفهم عن جماعات المجوس وإنكار عامتهم دار الإسلام أن تكون دارهم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ولتحقيق هذا الاسم لهم أيضا وجهان : إن كل ذى دين ومذهب نسب إلى المعنى الذى ادعاه لنفسه بحق الإسلام واليهودية والنصرانية ونحو هذا ، وكذلك المعتزلة يرون قدر أفعالهم لأنفسهم ، وغيرهم يرون ذلك منه ، فحال أن يشتهر به من رآه لغيره ، ويزال عمن يدعى حقيقته لنفسه ، وبمثله جاء عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في شرط الإيمان بالقدر خيره وشره من الله . والوجه الآخر الأمر المعروف الذى لم ير معتزليا سلم عما يزيل عنه اسم الإيمان والتحلى بحلية الإسلام من ارتكاب الكبائر بالشهوات مما يبين استخفافهم بدين الله واختيارهم الخروج منه بأدنى شهوة أعطوها لأنفسهم ، فهم أحق من ينسب إلى غير دين الله ، إذ هذا شأنهم في دينهم الذي هو عندهم دين الله ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم ذكر الكعبي أن ذلك من عادة العرب تلقيب من يلهج بشيء فيكثر ذكره في غير موضعه حتى يجاوز الحد فيه ونسبة ذلك إليه ، وهم يفعلون ذلك حتى قالوا في كل فاحشة وأمر ذميم هذا قدر الله. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : أخطأ فى هذا القدر من الدعوى من أوجه : أحدها ما حكى عن العرب ، والثانى ما حكى عنهم ، هم لا يقولون ذلك وإن كان يقوله.
God made the tongues of creation speak concerning them, their small and their great, those who know what the name contains or are ignorant, affirming that that became a nickname for them, not from where a human made in it, but by God's grace, so that the people of dhimma in religion may know by it, so they may beware of mixing with them. And they have in that two apparent signs: one of them in the color of each of them. Each of them has the cold paleness that eyes consider ugly, if that is compared to the faces of the Magians, they would find them equal. And the second is their staying away from the congregations of the Magians and the denial of their general population of the abode of Islam that it be their abode, and there is no power except by God. And for the verification of this name for them there are also two aspects: every possessor of a religion and sect is attributed to the meaning that he claimed for himself by right of Islam, Judaism, Christianity and the like, and likewise the Mu'tazila see the extent of their acts for themselves, and others see that from him, so it happens that one is famous by it from one who sees it for another, and removed from one who claims its reality for himself, and similar to that came from the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, concerning the condition of belief in destiny, its good and its evil, from God. And the other aspect is the well-known matter that no Mu'tazilite was seen safe from what removes from him the name of faith and adornment with the ornament of Islam, from committing major sins by desires, showing their contempt for the religion of God and their choice to leave it for the least desire they granted themselves, so they are more worthy to be attributed to other than the religion of God, since this is their state in their religion which for them is the religion of God, and there is no power except by God. Then al-Ka'bi mentioned that that is from the custom of the Arabs to nickname one who persists in something and mentions it frequently in other than its place until he exceeds the limit in it, and to attribute that to him, and they do that until they said about every immoral act and blameworthy matter: 'This is the decree of God.' The shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: He erred in this amount of claim in several aspects: one of them is what he narrated about the Arabs, and the second is what he narrated about them; they do not say that, even if he says it.
Source pages p. 915

Commentary
This passage explains the origin of the name 'Mu'tazila' and refutes a claim by al-Ka'bi. Maturidi begins by stating that God caused people to speak of the Mu'tazila by a certain name, which became a nickname for them, not by human invention but by divine grace, so that the People of the Book (ahl al-dhimma) may recognize them and avoid mixing with them. He mentions two visible signs (ʿilmān ẓāhirān) of the Mu'tazila: first, their pale complexion (ṣufra bārida) that is considered ugly, and when compared to Magians they look alike; second, their withdrawal from Magian congregations and their denial that the abode of Islam (dār al-islām) is their abode. Then he gives two aspects (wajhān) to verify the name: first, that every religious group is named by the meaning they claim for themselves (e.g., Muslims, Jews, Christians), and similarly the Mu'tazila see their own acts as coming from themselves, while others see them as coming from God, so the name sticks to those who hold that opinion and is removed from those who claim it falsely; this is supported by a hadith about belief in destiny. The second aspect is that no Mu'tazilite is seen safe from committing major sins (kabāʾir) due to desires, showing their contempt for religion, so they are more deserving to be attributed to a religion other than Islam. Finally, Maturidi reports that al-Ka'bi claimed that the name comes from the Arab custom of nicknaming someone who persists in mentioning something excessively, like saying 'this is the decree of God' about every evil act. The shaykh (Maturidi) refutes this, saying al-Ka'bi erred in two ways: what he narrated about the Arabs is false, and they do not say such things even if he says them.

Key Terms

العادة
العرب
التلقيب
القدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The name 'Mu'tazila' originated from the Arab custom of nicknaming someone who frequently mentions 'this is the decree of God'.
Correction: Maturidi refutes this, stating the custom and the saying are both false.

Checkpoint
What is the second error Maturidi points out about al-Ka'bi's claim?
A) The Arabs do not follow any customs.
B) The Arabs do not say 'this is the decree of God' for every evil act.
C) The Arabs only use nicknames for poets.
D) The Arabs never use the phrase 'this is the decree of God'.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's theory of the name's origin as historically inaccurate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ka'bi justified his claim by attributing a saying to 'the Arabs'. Maturidi rejected it as false. When you make claims about Islam or your faith, do you base them on reliable sources or do you repeat what 'everyone says'? Commit to verifying one belief today by checking its source.
?
This lesson shows how even respected figures can err in historical claims. Where in your own life have you relied on hearsay or 'common knowledge' about religious matters? Will you check the source before speaking again?
?
Maturidi didn't provide an alternative etymology; he simply refuted falsehood. Are you content to merely refute falsehood, or do you actively seek the truth? What step will you take today to learn the correct origin of a concept you've misunderstood?

The Prophet's Warning: Qadariyya and Murji'a
Maturidi introduces the hadith about Qadariyya and Murji'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the hadith about two groups not receiving intercession and how the names Qadariyya and Murji'a are understood in Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
The Prophet excluded two groups from his intercession: those who deny God's decree and those who defer all actions to God.

Imam Maturidi begins by exposing a deception: some try to associate the question with the Hashwiyya, but the terms Qadariyya and Murji'a are well-known in the ummah. He then cites a hadith from the Prophet that names these two groups as excluded from intercession. Understanding these labels is crucial for navigating the middle path in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how Maturidi starts by addressing a deceptive attribution, then moves to the hadith.
The hadith is the core of this lesson.
2
Identify the two groups
Find the names of the two groups mentioned in the hadith and note what each is characterized by.
Qadariyya is defined as those who deny God's decree.
3
Understand the hadith's import
The hadith is a warning. Reflect on why these two extremes are problematic.
They represent opposite errors.
4
Connect to the broader lesson
This sets up the need for a middle way, which Maturidi will define later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه : أما نسبة السؤال إلى الحشوية فإنما هو تمويههم ليروا أن الذى وإنما هذه التسمية متوارثة فى الأمة بأسرها، في خبر عن النبي عليه السلام: صنفان من أمتى لا تنالهم شفاعتي : القدرية والمرجئة، وفسرت القدرية بنفيهم القدر على الله. والأصل فى هذا أن المرجئة هى التى أرجت حقيقة أفعال الخلق إلى الله، والقدرية هي التي نفت عن الله تدبيرها، وجعلت كل التدبير فيها للخلق حتى معنى العالم، وبم على تدبير الخلق هم أفنوا وأبقوا وبه قام تدبير الله من البعث وأهل الجنة والنار، ليس لله فى ذلك إلا الإختبار، وكذا لا يحقق له في العالم أفعال سوى كونه بعد أن لم يكن. والعدل هو المذهب المتوسط بينها وذلك معنى قول الله عز وجل : وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُم أُمَّةً وَسَطًا، وقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : خير الأمور أوساطها.
The jurist said: As for attributing the question to the Hashwiyya, it is only their deception so that they may see that this designation is inherited in the entire ummah, in a report from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Two groups of my ummah will not receive my intercession: the Qadariyya and the Murji'a.' And the Qadariyya were interpreted as those who deny God's decree. The origin of this is that the Murji'a are those who defer the reality of the actions of creation to God, and the Qadariyya are those who deny His management of them, and make all management in them for creation, even the meaning of the world, and with what [؟] over the management of creation they annihilated and preserved, and by it God's management of the resurrection and the people of Paradise and Hell is established; God has only testing in that, and likewise no acts are verified for Him in the world except His existence after non-existence. Justice is the middle doctrine between them, and that is the meaning of God's saying: 'And thus We have made you a middle nation' (Quran 2:143), and the saying of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him: 'The best of affairs is their middle course.'
Source pages p. 917

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification passage. Maturidi begins by explaining that the attribution of the question to the Hashwiyya is a deceptive ploy, and that the designation 'Qadariyya' is inherited in the ummah based on a hadith in which the Prophet states that two groups will not receive his intercession: the Qadariyya and the Murji'a. The Qadariyya are defined as those who deny God's decree (al-qadar). Maturidi then clarifies the essential difference: the Murji'a defer the reality of all actions to God (i.e., extreme predestinarianism), while the Qadariyya deny God's management of actions and attribute all management to creation, even the meaning of the world. In their view, God's role is only testing, and He has no actual involvement in worldly events except His existence after non-existence. Maturidi then states that the just (al-ʿadl) doctrine is the middle path between these two extremes, citing Quran 2:143 and the hadith 'The best of affairs is their middle course.' This establishes the Islamic position of affirming both divine decree and human responsibility without falling into either extreme.

Key Terms
القدرية
المرجئة
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'Qadariyya' refers to those who affirm divine decree, but it actually refers to those who deny it.
Correction: The Qadariyya are those who deny God's decree, as Maturidi states: 'and the Qadariyya were interpreted as those who deny God's decree.'

Checkpoint
According to the hadith mentioned, which two groups will not receive the Prophet's intercession?
A) The Qadariyya and the Murji'a
B) The Qadariyya and the Jabriyya
C) The Murji'a and the Hashwiyya
D) The Qadariyya and the Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
The hadith warns that both predestinarian extremism (Murji'a) and denial of divine decree (Qadariyya) are dangerous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you tend more towards denying God's decree (by over-relying on your own efforts) or using His decree as an excuse (by neglecting responsibility)? Which tendency did the Prophet warn against more strongly in this hadith?
?
This hadith is a severe warning—no intercession for these two groups. How does that strike your heart? Are you willing to examine your own beliefs and actions today to ensure you are not falling into either extreme?

The Middle Way: Beyond Qadariyya and Murji'a
Maturidi defines Murji'a and Qadariyya and presents the middle way.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the contrasting views of Qadariyya and Murji'a regarding human action and divine management, and the middle doctrine that balances both.

Core Idea
The just path is to affirm both divine decree and human responsibility, avoiding the extremes of delegation and denial.

After citing the hadith, Maturidi explains the fundamental difference between the two sects: Murji'a defer all actions to God, while Qadariyya deny God's management entirely. He then presents the middle doctrine, supported by Quran and hadith, as the true Islamic position.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions
Pay attention to how Maturidi defines Murji'a and Qadariyya: one defers actions to God, the other denies God's involvement.
These definitions are the basis of the debate.
2
Analyze the extreme positions
Why is each extreme problematic? The Murji'a remove human responsibility; the Qadariyya remove divine power.
Both undermine Islamic theology.
3
Study the middle way
Maturidi states that justice is the middle doctrine. Note the Quranic and prophetic proofs he cites.
Quran 2:143 and the hadith 'The best of affairs is their middle course.'
4
Reflect on application
Consider how this middle path applies to understanding predestination and free will today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

Will you repent from that imbalance and strive for the middle way as taught by the Quran?

Definition of the Jabriyya Sect
Maturidi defines the Jabriyya sect and describes their denial of human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi defines the Jabriyya sect and their denial of human power.

Core Idea
The Jabriyya attribute all actions to God, leaving no real agency for humans.

Imam Maturidi now turns to define the second extreme sect in the qadar debate: the Jabriyya, who go to the opposite extreme from the Qadariyya. In this passage, he briefly but clearly marks their core claim—that all actions belong entirely to God and humans have no true power. Understanding this definition is essential for distinguishing the middle path of Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Notice the three key phrases: 'الذين يلقبوا بالجبر', 'أحالوا القدرة على ما في فعل جعل الله كاذبا', and 'أرجعوا جميع الأفعال إلى الله، ولم يثبتوا للعباد في التحقيق'.
The translation is tentative due to manuscript issues.
2
Identify the Jabriyya's view on power
The phrase 'أحالوا القدرة على ما في فعل جعل الله كاذبا' is obscure but likely means they denied human power in a way that implies God is unjust or lying. Reflect on why this is problematic.
3
Distinguish from the Qadariyya
Contrast the Jabriyya's total attribution of actions to God with the Qadariyya's extreme free will. Where do they differ?
This connects to the previous lesson.
4
Understand the consequence for human responsibility
If all actions are from God and humans have no real agency, then reward and punishment become meaningless. Ask yourself: why is this view rejected by Ahl al-Sunna?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الجبرية المعروفة عندنا هم الذين يلقبوا بالجبر، وأحالوا القدرة على ما في فعل جعل الله كاذبا، وأرجعوا جميع الأفعال إلى الله، ولم يثبتوا للعباد في التحقيق
Then the Jabriyya known among us are those who are labeled as Jabr (compulsion), and they referred power [؟] to what is in the act of making God a liar, and they attributed all actions to God, and they did not establish for the servants in reality [؟]
Source pages p. 918

Commentary
This passage is a brief definition of the Jabriyya sect (the 'compulsionists'). Maturidi states that they are known among us as those who are labeled with 'Jabr' (which means compulsion). He then describes their doctrine: they referred power (al-qudra) to something that makes God a liar? The phrase is unclear but likely means they denied human power entirely, attributing all actions to God. They did not establish any real agency for the servants. This completes the trilogy of sects: Qadariyya (extreme free will), Jabriyya (extreme predestination), and the middle way (Ahl al-Sunna). The passage is incomplete in the manuscript but conveys the essential identification.

Key Terms
الجبرية
الجبر
القدرة
الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Jabriyya's view is the same as the Sunni view of predestination.
Correction: While both affirm divine decree, Jabriyya deny human power entirely, leading to fatalism and denying moral responsibility. Ahl al-Sunna affirm both divine decree and human acquisition (kasb).

Checkpoint
What is the defining characteristic of the Jabriyya according to Maturidi?
A) They deny divine decree
B) They attribute all actions to God and deny real human agency
C) They affirm free will
D) They reject predestination

Key Takeaway
Maturidi defines the Jabriyya as those who strip humans of any real power, attributing all actions solely to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking 'God made me do it' or 'it was my fate'? If you really believed that, how could you genuinely repent? What would you need to ask God for forgiveness?
?
If all actions are from God as the Jabriyya claim, then gratitude and blame lose meaning. Think of a specific good deed you did recently. Did you thank God for enabling it, or did you only credit yourself? How would your prayer change if you remembered that your own power is never the sole cause?
?
Maturidi warns that the Jabriyya's position leads to making God a liar. Where in your life do you subtly accuse God of being unfair—by complaining about your circumstances or blaming Him for your mistakes? Will you now actively reject that thought and accept full responsibility for your choices?

The Qadariyya's Proof from 'Take It with Strength'
Maturidi refutes the Qadariyya's proof from 'Take it with strength'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the Qadariyya's claim that power must precede action, using the Quranic verse 'Take it with strength' and the principle that strength is concurrent with the action.

Core Idea
Power is not pre-existent but arises with the action itself.

The Qadariyya argued that human power must exist before the act, citing the verse 'Take it with strength.' In this lesson, we see Maturidi's response: the verse speaks of strength at the moment of taking, not before. He uses a simple linguistic example to show that commands like 'take it with your hands' imply simultaneity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qadariyya's argument and Maturidi's initial response
Read the first part of the passage where Maturidi presents the Qadariyya's proof from the verse and begins his refutation.
2
Analyze the interpretation of 'strength' as concurrent
Focus on Maturidi's explanation that 'strength' in the verse refers to the time of taking, and his analogy of 'take it with your hands' to demonstrate simultaneity.
3
Consider the example of 'take it with your hands' as proof of simultaneity
Reflect on how the command implies that the hands (strength) are present at the moment of the action, not before.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى عن بني مروان وحكى عن الذين برأوا المذنبين، وحملوا ذلك على ما ذكر [؟] إيجاب القدر للعباد كذب كله، فنعوذ بالله من الحيرة في الدين الحاملة على [؟] المسلمين. ثم احتجت القدرية في تقديم القدرة على الفعل بأي من كتاب الله تعالى، منها قوله: "فَخُذْهَا بِقُوَّةٍ"، وقال أهل التأويل: فاعمل بها تجد [؟] فكأنهم رأوا القوة هاهنا الأسباب، لكن الظاهر من ذلك قولنا: خذها بقوة، أي وقت الأخذ؛ لأنها إذا لم تكن في وقت الأخذ يكون الأخذ بلا قوة، ثبت به الذي يذهب، كمن يقول لآخر: خذه بيديك وانظر إليه ببصرك، فهو على الالتقاء، وعلى ذلك قوله لموسى: فَخُذْهَا بِقُوَّةٍ وَأْمُرْ قَوْمَكَ يَأْخُذُوا بِأَحْسَنِها، واحتجوا أيضا بقول الجني: وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيٌّ أَمِين، وقول المرأة: إِنَّ خَيْرَ مَنِ اسْتَأْجَرْتَ الْقَوِيُّ الْأَمِين. قال الشيخ رحمه الله: والحرفان مما ليس لهم التعلق به لما كانت قوة موسى التي علمت بها إنما علمت وقت النزح، وهي لا تبقى إلى ذلك الوقت، وكذلك قوة الجني على ما امتحن نفسه فيما سبق، والله الموفق. والثاني على إرادة وقت الاستعمال بالعادة الجارية بالحدوث في كل وقت لما شاء، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
It is narrated from Banu Marwan and he related from those who absolved the sinners, and they attributed that to what was mentioned [?] the imposition of predestination upon servants, all of it false. So we seek refuge with Allah from confusion in religion that leads to reviling Muslims. Then the Qadariyya argued for the precedence of power over action from some of the book of Allah Almighty. Among it is His saying: 'Take it with strength.' The people of interpretation said: Act upon it and you will find [?]—they thought that 'strength' here means means, but the apparent meaning from that is our saying: Take it with strength, i.e., at the time of taking; because if it is not at the time of taking, the taking is without strength. This is established by the one who goes, like one who says to another: Take it with your hands and look at it with your eyes—this is about conjunction. And similarly His saying to Moses: 'Take it with strength and command your people to take the best of it.' They also argued by the saying of the jinn: 'Indeed, I am strong and trustworthy over it,' and the saying of the woman: 'Indeed, the best one you hire is the strong and trustworthy.' The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The two phrases are not relevant to them, because the strength of Moses that was known was only known at the time of drawing water, and it does not remain until that time. Likewise, the strength of the jinn was based on what he tested of himself previously. And Allah is the giver of success. The second [interpretation] is about intending the time of use, according to the habitual occurrence of coming into being at every time whenever He wills. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 918

Commentary
This passage refutes the Qadariyya's argument that power (قدرة) must exist before the action, based on Quranic verses. Maturidi begins by citing a tradition about Banu Marwan and those who absolve sinners, then states that the Qadariyya argued from verses like 'Take it with strength' (Quran 7:145). The interpreters understood 'strength' as means, but the apparent meaning is about the time of taking—the strength is concurrent with the act, not pre-existing. Maturidi uses the example of someone saying 'take it with your hands' to show the immediacy. He then addresses the objection from the story of Moses (Quran 7:145) where 'strength' might be seen as pre-existent, but explains that Moses' strength was only known at the time of drawing water and did not persist. Similarly, the jinni's testimony about his strength (Quran 27:39) refers to a past test, not a pre-existing power. Maturidi concludes that the second interpretation points to the habitual creation of power at the time of action, emphasizing that all power is from Allah.

Key Terms
قدرية
قدرة
قوة
أهل التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'strength' in the verse is often misinterpreted as pre-existent power.
Correction: It actually refers to power concurrent with the action, not before.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does 'strength' (قوة) in the verse 'Take it with strength' refer to?
A) Pre-existing power before the action
B) Power at the time of taking the action
C) The means and instruments
D) The strength of faith

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya's proof from 'Take it with strength' fails because the verse indicates power simultaneous with the action, not pre-existent power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you tell yourself that you had the power to avoid it before the action, or that the power came at the moment of temptation? How does Maturidi's understanding of concurrent power change your sense of accountability before Allah?
?
If power is simultaneous with action, what does that mean for your view of divine predestination? Are you willing to accept that your power is not independent but given by Allah at the very moment you act, and that this does not diminish your responsibility?
?
The Qadariyya wanted to protect human responsibility by arguing for pre-existent power. Maturidi shows another way. Where do you truly place your trust: in your own pre-existing abilities or in Allah's grant of power at each moment? Let this lesson move you to gratitude for every act you perform, recognizing that Allah enabled it.

Refuting the Qadariyya with the Examples of Moses and the Jinn
Maturidi refutes the Qadariyya's proofs from Moses and the jinn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the Qadariyya's further proofs from the stories of Moses and the jinn, and his conclusion that power is created at the time of action.

Core Idea
Neither Moses' strength nor the jinn's strength proves pre-existent power.

The Qadariyya also cited the examples of Moses' strength when drawing water and the jinni's claim to be strong. Maturidi explains that these refer to specific moments in the past, not a general principle of power preceding action. He concludes that power is created habitually at the time of action, emphasizing that all power is from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Examine the Qadariyya's use of Moses' story
Read the part where the Qadariyya cite the jinn's and woman's statements as proofs.
2
Analyze Maturidi's response about the timing of Moses' strength
Notice how Maturidi says Moses' strength was only known at the time of drawing water, not before.
3
Consider the jinn's example and the conclusion
Understand that the jinn's strength was based on a past test, and then Maturidi concludes that power is created habitually at the time of action.

The Incoherence of Absolute Compulsion (Jabr)
Maturidi refutes the Jabariyya by exposing the absurd consequences of their denial of human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Jabariyya view (absolute compulsion) leads to logical absurdities and undermines the purpose of revelation.

Core Idea
If God is the sole agent, then His commands are meaningless.

Imam al-Maturidi refutes the Jabariyya who deny human power entirely. He shows that their position forces God into contradictions: He would be commanding Himself, forbidding Himself, and punishing others for acts He causes. This not only destroys the meaning of prophets and scriptures but also makes creation futile. This passage is a powerful argument that absolute compulsion is incompatible with divine wisdom and justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the Jabariyya description
Read the Arabic passage once to understand how Maturidi defines the Jabariyya: they deny any effective act to servants and attribute all actions to God.
Note the key terms: جبرية, قدرة, فعل.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Maturidi shows the consequences: if God is the only agent, then His commands become reflexive—He commands Himself, forbids Himself, and punishes others for what He does. This makes His wisdom and mercy meaningless.
Notice how this destroys the purpose of sending prophets and books.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that such a view describes a devil, not the All-Wise Creator. Consider how this argument preserves the meaning of human responsibility and divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد احتجوا بما في القرآن من ذكر الاستطاعة، وقد بينا ذلك الوجه، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم الجبرية المعروفة عندنا هم الذين يلقبوا بالجبر، وأحالوا القدرة على ما في فعل جعل الله كاذبا، وأرجعوا جميع الأفعال إلى الله، ولم يثبتوا للعباد في التحقيق فعلا. قيل: يقول لهم الله: لم فعلتم ذا، ولم لا فعلتم ذا؟ ونقول: افعلوا ذا، ولا تفعلوا ذا في التحقيق، بل إن أمر أو نهى فإنما يأمر في التحقيق نفسه وينهى نفسه، ثم هو يرتكب المنهي في التحقيق، ويأمر ويطيع هو في الحقيقة، يعاقب غيره فيعذبه ويثيبه، ويسميه مع هذا حكيما رحيما جل من صفته الرحمة والحكمة، وعلى ذلك يجب أن لا يجدوا الألم في الحقيقة واللذة، وتكون حقيقتها راجعة إلى الله جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى. ثم يبطل معنى الرسل والكتب في التحصيل تصير إلى الله بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، لا منه إلى غيره ثم يبطل حكمة خلق الخلق ويحصل على العبث إن كان العلم يبلغ معرفته، ومن يكون خروج فعله على كفران وجحود المنن، والكذب في الإخبار، والسفه في الأفعال فهو حقيق أن يكون شيطانا رجيما، فهو كذلك لا ريب فيه، وهو ما شبيه بقولهم: كان الله غير عالم ولا قادر، ثم صار كذلك، فلعل تدبيره الأفعال التي كانت فما نسب إلى الخلق في ذلك الوقت جل الله وتعالى عن ذلك وهم الذين يلقبوا بالاعتزال - الخبر إلينا، على تبرينا كما ثم نسب القدرية عن ذلك عقدا وقولا، لكن كتبهم في هذا نحو كذبهم علينا في اسم القدرية ثم تذكر أحقنا ذلك في مقابلة المذهبين؛ ليعلموا جرأة المعتزلة وعظيم سفههم بينا في القدرية - وادعوا علينا اسم الجبر بانكارنا كون قدرة الفعل قبل وقته، ثم هم حققوا الفعل في وقت لا قدرة فيه، وتحقيق الفعل في وقت الوصف بلا قدرة أقرب إلى معنى الجبر من تحقيقها مع الفعل لمن عقل الجبر والاختيار. ومما يوضح ذلك أن الفعل غير متوهم في حال العجز، ومتوهم وجوده في حال ارتفاع العجز، فكان توهمه مع الارتفاع أرفع وأبلغ من توهمه مع الوجود؛ إذ هو سبب، فكذلك القدرة التي هي سبب الفعل في الحقيقة، ويؤيد ذلك فساد الدرك مع ذهابه بما تقدم من البصر، وكذا السمع وعمل كل الحواس، فلذلك المنع بالبصر
And they also argued by what is in the Quran of mention of capability (استطاعة), and we have already explained that aspect. And there is no power except with Allah. Then the Jabariyya known among us are those who are labeled with jabr (compulsion), and they attributed power to that [i.e., they denied power to the servant] and made God a liar in [His] action, and they referred all actions to God, and they did not affirm for the servants any effective act. It is said: God would say to them: Why did you do this? And why did you not do this? And we say: Do this, and do not do this, in reality—but rather, if He commands or forbids, He only commands in reality Himself and forbids Himself, then He commits the forbidden in reality, and He commands and obeys in truth, and He punishes others and torments them and rewards them, and He calls Himself wise and merciful—glory be to Him whose attributes are mercy and wisdom. According to that, they should not feel pain in reality nor pleasure, and their reality would revert to God—glory be to Allah above that and exalted. Then the meaning of messengers and books would be nullified in effect, turning to God in command, prohibition, promise, and threat—not from Him to others. Then the wisdom of creating creation would be nullified, and it would result in futility, if knowledge could attain His knowledge. And whoever's action results in ingratitude and denial of favors, and lying in reports, and foolishness in actions, he is worthy to be an accursed devil. He is thus without doubt. And this resembles their saying: Allah was not knowing nor powerful, then He became so. Perhaps His management of actions that were and then were attributed to creation at that time—glory be to Allah and exalted above that. And they are the ones who are labeled as Mu'tazila—the report reaching us concerning our exoneration—as also. Then the Qadariyya labeled us concerning that as belief and saying, but their books in this are like their lying about us in the name Qadariyya. Then we mentioned our proof (?) in opposition to the two schools, so that they may know the audacity of the Mu'tazila and the greatness of their foolishness among the Qadariyya—and they claimed against us the name of Jabriyya because of our denial that power of action exists before its time, but they realized the action at a time when there is no power. And realizing the action at the time of description without power is closer to the meaning of jabr than realizing it with action, for one who understands jabr and choice. And what clarifies that is that action is not conceivable in a state of incapacity, while its existence is conceivable in a state of removal of incapacity, so conceiving it with removal is higher and more profound than conceiving it with existence, because it is a cause. Likewise, power which is the cause of action in reality, and that is supported by the corruption of perception with its removal as preceded with sight, and likewise hearing and the operation of all senses. Therefore, the prevention is with sight.
Source pages p. 918

Commentary
This passage refutes the Jabariyya (those who affirm absolute compulsion) and clarifies the mislabeling of sects. Maturidi begins by noting that the Qadariyya also argued from Quranic mentions of capability, but this is already addressed. Then he describes the Jabariyya as those who deny any effective action to servants, attributing all acts to God, which leads to contradictions: if God commands or forbids but is the sole agent, then He commands Himself, forbids Himself, commits the forbidden, and punishes others—making God inconsistent with wisdom and mercy. This nullifies the purpose of messengers, books, and the wisdom of creation, leading to absurdity. Such a view is comparable to saying God was not knowing or powerful then became so. Then Maturidi discusses the naming: the Mu'tazila claim that Ahl al-Sunna are Jabariyya because they deny power before the act, but in fact the Mu'tazila themselves realize the action at a time when there is no power (since they claim power precedes but does not last), which is closer to jabr. Moreover, action is inconceivable during incapacity, but conceivable when incapacity is removed—so power as a cause is valid. This is analogous to how senses function. The passage ends with a note about perception with sight.

Key Terms
جبرية
قدرة
فعل
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Jabariyya believe that affirming God's absolute power requires denying all human agency.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this leads to absurdities; true belief affirms both God's power and human acquisition.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is one consequence of the Jabariyya's denial of human power?
A) It affirms God's wisdom and mercy
B) It nullifies the meaning of messengers and books
C) It proves human freedom
D) It leads to denial of God's existence

Key Takeaway
The Jabariyya's absolute compulsion leads to absurdities that contradict divine wisdom and the purpose of revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'God made me do it' or using divine decree as an excuse? How does this passage force you to take full responsibility for your actions? Commit today to sincerely repent without blaming anyone else.
?
Do you truly believe that God's commands and prohibitions are meaningful and require your genuine response? How would your daily worship change if you acted as if your choices truly matter to God?
?
If you fully internalized that God is infinitely wise and just, how would it affect your view of the trials you face? Are you willing to accept personal accountability for your reactions instead of attributing them to fate?
