Defining Kufr and Iman: The Major Sinner is a Believer
Maturidi defines kufr and iman to prove major sinner is a believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's definition of kufr as denial and covering, and iman as affirmation, and why a major sinner is therefore a believer.

Core Idea
Kufr is denial or covering; a major sinner does neither, so he is a believer by affirmation.

After exposing the contradiction, Maturidi now explains what kufr and iman truly mean. Using both common usage (al-'urf) and the literal sense, he shows that kufr is either denial (takdhib) or covering (sitr), while iman is affirmation (tasdiq). Since the major sinner affirms God, hopes for His mercy, and does not cover His blessings, he cannot be a disbeliever, and must be a believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage then its translation. Note the definitions and the reasoning steps.
The passage contains two arguments: one from 'urf (common usage) and one from haqiqa (reality).
2
Identify the two definitions of kufr
First, in common usage (al-'urf), kufr means denial (takdhib). Second, in reality (al-haqiqa), kufr means covering (sitr). The author shows neither applies to the major sinner.
The sinner is not a denier; he affirms and hopes. He also does not cover God's blessings.
3
Understand the definition of iman
Iman in both 'urf and revelation (sam') is affirmation (tasdiq). Since the sinner affirms God and has not denied anything, he is a believer.
This directly counters the Mu'tazilite intermediate position.
4
Appreciate the conclusion
The passage concludes that it is established that the major sinner is a believer. The Mu'tazila cannot claim he is a disbeliever or in between.
Maturidi's definitions are key to the Sunni position.

Source Text

The First Refutation: The Khawarij Contradict Themselves
First argument: self-contradiction of Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Khawarij and Mu'tazila contradict themselves by labeling major sinners as disbelievers while the Quran reserves despair of mercy for actual disbelievers.

Core Idea
Calling a sinner a disbeliever implies they deserve eternal punishment, but that contradicts divine mercy.

This lesson examines the first of three arguments against the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, who claim that any Muslim who commits a major sin becomes an eternal dweller of Hell. The argument exposes a logical contradiction in their position, using Quranic verses to show that they effectively call the sinner a disbeliever—yet the Quran states that only disbelievers truly despair of God's mercy, while believers maintain hope.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the structure: the Khawarij claim, the Quranic response, and the conclusion.
Pay attention to the quotation of Quran 29:23.
2
Identify the contradiction
The Khawarij call the sinner a disbeliever, but the Quran says disbelievers despair of mercy. The sinner, however, does not despair—so they cannot be labeled as such.
3
Understand the proper stance
Believers describe God as Pardoning and Merciful and hope for His forgiveness, without testifying to a specific outcome for any individual sinner.
The passage ends with 'We will assign him what he has turned to' – a reference to Quran 4:115.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الحق أن يقال: جميع الخوارج والمعتزلة عند ارتكابهم الكبائر كفرة على قولهم، مستوجبون للخلود في النار، وغيرهم من أصناف منتحلي الإسلام لأوجه: أحدها أنهم أجمعوا على من رحمه الله، وذلك وصف الكفر بما ذكر من الآية وبقوله: وَالَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِآيَاتِ اللهِ وَلِقَائِهِ أُولَئِكَ يَئِسُوا مِنْ رَحْمَتِي، فلزم الفريقين اسم الكفر والخلود في النار. وأما المؤمنون بآيات الله وصفوه عفوا غفورا رحيما محققين لذلك، فهم لهم الرجاء، ولا يجوز لهم الشهادة بواحد من الأمرين، فتولى كل قول كما قال الله تعالى: نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى وَنُصْلِهِ جَهَنَّمَ، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثاني أنهم جميعا ضيقوا رحمة الله فجعلوها بحيث لا تتسع لذنب؛ إذ الذنوب التي ليست بكبائر لا يجوز معها التعذيب، فليس لرحمة الله فيما ليس له التعذيب ولا لعفوه فيما استغنى عنه بالحكمة، وجعلوا الغضب والسخط كل ذنب في الحكمة يجوز له التعذيب، فلا عفو إذا على قولهم ولا رحمة، فحق هذا القول الحرمان. وأما من يصفه بسعة الرحمة وعظيم العفو فحق له المغفرة والعفو؛ لأن كل كريم يوصف بهذا، فهو أميل له من الوصف له بما وصفته الخوارج والمعتزلة، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثالث قال الله تعالى: إِنْ يَنْتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُمْ مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ، ولا يجوز أن يكون الذي به الانتهاء غير محدود ولا معروف الوصول إلى جميع الطاعات والقيام بجميع الأمور بتأخر الحياة على قول الخوارج فتصير بحيث لا انتهاء له، وكذلك على قول المعتزلة، فثبت أن الانتهاء هو الذي يملكه كله في كل وقت، وهو البرء عن كل أنواع الكفر والمعاصي، والإيمان بالله تعالى وبجميع ما يؤمن المرء به، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the truth is to say: All the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, according to their claim when they commit major sins, are disbelievers, deserving eternal abiding in the Fire. And others among the sects of those who claim Islam [differ] for aspects: The first is that they all agreed upon [applying] 'whom Allah has mercy'? and that is describing disbelief with what was mentioned in the verse and His saying: 'And those who disbelieve in the signs of Allah and the meeting with Him, those have despaired of My mercy.' So the name of disbelief and eternal abiding in the Fire necessarily applies to both groups. As for those who believe in Allah's signs and describe Him as Pardoning, Forgiving, Merciful, realizing that, they have hope for them, and they are not permitted to testify for either of the two matters. So each claim will be assigned as Allah said: 'We will assign him what he has turned to and expose him to Hell.' And there is no power except with Allah. The second: They all restricted Allah's mercy and made such that it does not encompass any sin; since sins that are not major cannot be punished, there is no room for mercy regarding what punishment is not for, nor for forgiveness regarding what wisdom renders superfluous. They made anger and wrath [apply to] every sin that wisdom permits punishment for. So there is no forgiveness on their saying, nor mercy. So the right of this saying is deprivation. As for the one who describes Him with vast mercy and great pardon, then forgiveness and pardon are his due because every generous one described thus is more inclined to that than to the description with which the Khawarij and Mu'tazila describe Him. And there is no power except with Allah. The third: Allah said: 'If they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them.' And it is not permissible that the one by whom desistance occurs be unlimited or that reaching all acts of obedience and performing all matters be known [only] after a delay of life according to the saying of the Khawarij, for then it would become such that there is no desistance from it. Similarly, according to the saying of the Mu'tazila. So it is established that desistance is that which one has full control over at all times, and it is disavowal of all kinds of disbelief and sins, and faith in Allah Most High and in all that one believes in. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 934

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments (wujuh) against the Khawarij and Mu'tazila who claim that major sinners are eternally punished. The first argument uses the Ahwaz? Actually, the text says 'all the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, according to their claim, are disbelievers' – this seems ironic: they themselves apply the label kafir to sinners, but the Quran says only disbelievers despair of mercy. So they contradict themselves: they describe the sinner as a disbeliever (thus deserving eternal punishment), but the Quran says only disbelievers despair—yet sinners hope for mercy. So the Khawarij and Mu'tazila end up implicitly associating the sinner with disbelief. The author then contrasts the proper attitude: believers describe God as forgiving and merciful and maintain hope, without testifying to either eternal punishment or forgiveness for a specific individual—they leave the matter to God. The second argument: the Khawarij and Mu'tazila restrict God's mercy by saying that minor sins are not punishable (so there is no need for mercy there) and major sins are always punished (so no mercy there either), thus removing mercy altogether. But one who truly knows God as generous must attribute vast mercy and forgiveness to Him. The third argument concerns the condition of desistance (al-intiha') that triggers forgiveness according to Quran 8:38. The Khawarij and Mu'tazila make desistance impossible by requiring absolute obedience that cannot be achieved in a limited lifespan, or by making it contingent on future actions unknown. In reality, desistance means stopping from all disbelief and sins at any time, which is within human capacity through faith and repentance.

Key Terms
خلود
نار
رحمة
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, what label do the Khawarij and Mu'tazila apply to major sinners?
A) Disbelievers
B) Hypocrites
C) Sinners but not disbelievers
D) Forgiven

Key Takeaway
Calling a major sinner a disbeliever contradicts the Quran, which ties despair of mercy only to true disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you ever, even in your heart, consider them beyond hope? This lesson forces you to examine that. Will you now actively guard against such judgment and instead hope for their mercy, as the Sunnah teaches?
?
The Khawarij thought they were upholding justice, but they fell into contradiction. Are there areas in your own life where you apply a rigid, unforgiving standard to others that you do not apply to yourself? How will you realign that with the Quranic emphasis on Allah's mercy?
?
This lesson says the sinner hopes for mercy even while sinning. Have you ever committed a sin while telling yourself 'Allah is forgiving'? That is hope. But does that hope excuse you from repentance and change? Reflect: Are you using hope as a license to persist in sin, or does it drive you to turn back to Allah?

The Second Refutation: Restricting Divine Mercy
Second argument: elimination of mercy by restricting its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Khawarij and Mu'tazila effectively deny God's mercy by making it inapplicable to both minor and major sins.

Core Idea
If mercy applies to no sin, then it is not mercy at all.

The second argument shifts focus to the nature of God's mercy. Maturidi demonstrates that the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, by their own logic, eliminate divine mercy entirely: minor sins are not punished (so no mercy needed), and major sins are always punished (so mercy excluded). This leaves no room for forgiveness or mercy, contradicting God's attribute of vast mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read carefully how the Khawarij/Mu'tazila divide sins into minor (not punished) and major (always punished), leaving no sin for which mercy can apply.
Note the terms 'ghadab' (anger) and 'sakht' (wrath) for major sins.
2
Analyze the logic
If minor sins are not punishable, there is no need for mercy or forgiveness. If major sins are always punished, mercy cannot apply. So their system has no mercy.
3
Contrast with the correct view
The true believer describes God with vast mercy and great pardon, which is fitting for a generous Lord.
The passage ends by affirming that this description is more appropriate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الحق أن يقال: جميع الخوارج والمعتزلة عند ارتكابهم الكبائر كفرة على قولهم، مستوجبون للخلود في النار، وغيرهم من أصناف منتحلي الإسلام لأوجه: أحدها أنهم أجمعوا على من رحمه الله، وذلك وصف الكفر بما ذكر من الآية وبقوله: وَالَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِآيَاتِ اللهِ وَلِقَائِهِ أُولَئِكَ يَئِسُوا مِنْ رَحْمَتِي، فلزم الفريقين اسم الكفر والخلود في النار. وأما المؤمنون بآيات الله وصفوه عفوا غفورا رحيما محققين لذلك، فهم لهم الرجاء، ولا يجوز لهم الشهادة بواحد من الأمرين، فتولى كل قول كما قال الله تعالى: نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى وَنُصْلِهِ جَهَنَّمَ، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثاني أنهم جميعا ضيقوا رحمة الله فجعلوها بحيث لا تتسع لذنب؛ إذ الذنوب التي ليست بكبائر لا يجوز معها التعذيب، فليس لرحمة الله فيما ليس له التعذيب ولا لعفوه فيما استغنى عنه بالحكمة، وجعلوا الغضب والسخط كل ذنب في الحكمة يجوز له التعذيب، فلا عفو إذا على قولهم ولا رحمة، فحق هذا القول الحرمان. وأما من يصفه بسعة الرحمة وعظيم العفو فحق له المغفرة والعفو؛ لأن كل كريم يوصف بهذا، فهو أميل له من الوصف له بما وصفته الخوارج والمعتزلة، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثالث قال الله تعالى: إِنْ يَنْتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُمْ مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ، ولا يجوز أن يكون الذي به الانتهاء غير محدود ولا معروف الوصول إلى جميع الطاعات والقيام بجميع الأمور بتأخر الحياة على قول الخوارج فتصير بحيث لا انتهاء له، وكذلك على قول المعتزلة، فثبت أن الانتهاء هو الذي يملكه كله في كل وقت، وهو البرء عن كل أنواع الكفر والمعاصي، والإيمان بالله تعالى وبجميع ما يؤمن المرء به، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the truth is to say: All the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, according to their claim when they commit major sins, are disbelievers, deserving eternal abiding in the Fire. And others among the sects of those who claim Islam [differ] for aspects: The first is that they all agreed upon [applying] 'whom Allah has mercy'? and that is describing disbelief with what was mentioned in the verse and His saying: 'And those who disbelieve in the signs of Allah and the meeting with Him, those have despaired of My mercy.' So the name of disbelief and eternal abiding in the Fire necessarily applies to both groups. As for those who believe in Allah's signs and describe Him as Pardoning, Forgiving, Merciful, realizing that, they have hope for them, and they are not permitted to testify for either of the two matters. So each claim will be assigned as Allah said: 'We will assign him what he has turned to and expose him to Hell.' And there is no power except with Allah. The second: They all restricted Allah's mercy and made such that it does not encompass any sin; since sins that are not major cannot be punished, there is no room for mercy regarding what punishment is not for, nor for forgiveness regarding what wisdom renders superfluous. They made anger and wrath [apply to] every sin that wisdom permits punishment for. So there is no forgiveness on their saying, nor mercy. So the right of this saying is deprivation. As for the one who describes Him with vast mercy and great pardon, then forgiveness and pardon are his due because every generous one described thus is more inclined to that than to the description with which the Khawarij and Mu'tazila describe Him. And there is no power except with Allah. The third: Allah said: 'If they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them.' And it is not permissible that the one by whom desistance occurs be unlimited or that reaching all acts of obedience and performing all matters be known [only] after a delay of life according to the saying of the Khawarij, for then it would become such that there is no desistance from it. Similarly, according to the saying of the Mu'tazila. So it is established that desistance is that which one has full control over at all times, and it is disavowal of all kinds of disbelief and sins, and faith in Allah Most High and in all that one believes in. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 934

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments (wujuh) against the Khawarij and Mu'tazila who claim that major sinners are eternally punished. The first argument uses the Ahwaz? Actually, the text says 'all the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, according to their claim, are disbelievers' – this seems ironic: they themselves apply the label kafir to sinners, but the Quran says only disbelievers despair of mercy. So they contradict themselves: they describe the sinner as a disbeliever (thus deserving eternal punishment), but the Quran says only disbelievers despair—yet sinners hope for mercy. So the Khawarij and Mu'tazila end up implicitly associating the sinner with disbelief. The author then contrasts the proper attitude: believers describe God as forgiving and merciful and maintain hope, without testifying to either eternal punishment or forgiveness for a specific individual—they leave the matter to God. The second argument: the Khawarij and Mu'tazila restrict God's mercy by saying that minor sins are not punishable (so there is no need for mercy there) and major sins are always punished (so no mercy there either), thus removing mercy altogether. But one who truly knows God as generous must attribute vast mercy and forgiveness to Him. The third argument concerns the condition of desistance (al-intiha') that triggers forgiveness according to Quran 8:38. The Khawarij and Mu'tazila make desistance impossible by requiring absolute obedience that cannot be achieved in a limited lifespan, or by making it contingent on future actions unknown. In reality, desistance means stopping from all disbelief and sins at any time, which is within human capacity through faith and repentance.

Key Terms
رحمة
عفو
غضب
سخط
حكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's mercy only covers minor sins, while major sins are exclusively subject to wrath.
Correction: This passage shows that such a view eliminates mercy entirely; God's mercy is vast and can encompass any sin.

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, what happens to divine mercy in the view of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila?
A) It is restricted to minor sins only
B) It is eliminated entirely
C) It is greater than their description
D) It applies to all sins equally

Key Takeaway
By making mercy inapplicable to both minor and major sins, the Khawarij and Mu'tazila deny God's attribute of vast mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you instinctively assume it is 'too small' to matter or 'too big' to be forgiven? How does this lesson expose that both assumptions deny God's vast mercy? Repent of the sin you have been ignoring or despairing of right now.
?
Where in your heart have you imposed human logic on God's mercy, deciding that some sins are beyond forgiveness or too trivial to need it? This lesson shows that such logic nullifies mercy. What specific sin do you need to bring before His vast mercy today?
?
If you truly believed that God's mercy encompasses every sin without exception, how would that change the way you approach your own faults and the faults of others? What is holding you back from embracing that expansive mercy right now?

The Third Refutation: The Reality of Desistance (Intiha')
Third argument: correct understanding of desistance (intiha').

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Khawarij and Mu'tazila misunderstand the Quranic condition of 'desistance' (intiha') required for forgiveness, and how true desistance is possible through faith and repentance.

Core Idea
Desistance from sin is always possible through faith and repentance; it does not require perfect obedience.

The final argument centers on the Quranic verse 'if they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them' (8:38). Maturidi critiques the Khawarij and Mu'tazila for making desistance impossible: either by requiring perfect obedience beyond human capacity or by placing it in the unknowable future. In reality, desistance is a simple act of turning away from sin and embracing faith, which is within everyone's power at any moment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read how the Quranic condition of desistance is presented, and how the Khawarij and Mu'tazila distort it.
The verse key is Quran 8:38.
2
Understand the Khawarij error
The Khawarij think desistance requires unlimited time to achieve all obedience, making it impossible in a finite life.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila error
The Mu'tazila also make desistance contingent on future actions, rendering it unknowable and unattainable.
4
Learn the correct meaning
True desistance is full control over stopping all sins at any time, and it consists of disavowing disbelief and sins, and having faith in Allah.
This is within human capability through sincere repentance.

Three Arguments Refuting Khawarij and Mu'tazila on Eternal Punishment
Maturidi enumerates three arguments refuting Khawarij and Mu'tazila on eternal punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's three arguments that refute the claims of Khawarij and Mu'tazila regarding eternal punishment and the scope of God's mercy.

Core Idea
Eternal punishment applies only to disbelief, not major sins, because God's mercy is vast.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi directly engages with the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, who both held that major sinners deserve eternal punishment. He presents three logical and scriptural arguments to show the inconsistency of their position, emphasizing God's boundless mercy and the true meaning of repentance. Understanding these arguments helps clarify the Sunni doctrine of forgiveness for major sins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three arguments
Read the passage and locate the three 'أوجه' (aspects/arguments). Notice how each is introduced (أحدها, والثاني, والثالث).
The arguments are presented sequentially; the first is based on consensus, the second on mercy, the third on the Quranic promise.
2
Analyze the first argument
Examine how Maturidi argues that both Khawarij and Mu'tazila apply the name of disbelief to themselves by agreeing on despair of mercy, thus making eternity binding on both groups.
He uses Quran 29:23 to show that despair of mercy is a trait of disbelievers.
3
Analyze the second argument
Understand how Maturidi accuses both groups of restricting God's mercy. If mercy does not cover sins, then there is no forgiveness, contradicting God's attributes of vast mercy and pardon.
This argument highlights the logical consequence of their view: they negate God's mercy.
4
Analyze the third argument
See how Maturidi uses Quran 8:38 to show that desisting from disbelief leads to forgiveness, and argues that true 'desisting' is complete repentance and faith, which is possible at any time.
This refutes the Mu'tazilite idea of a middle station and shows that a major sinner who repents is forgiven.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the final statement that on the Mu'tazilite view, the committer of a major sin must be forgiven, thus their claim of universal eternity is invalid.
Maturidi turns their own logic against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولهم كتاب التوحيد ، مستوجبون للخلود في النار ، وغيرهم من أصناف منتحلى الإسلام لأوجه : أحدها أنهم أجمعوا على من رحمه الله ، وذلك وصف الكفر بما ذكر من الآية وبقوله : " وَالَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِآيَاتِ اللهِ وَلِقَائِهِ أُولَئِكَ يَئِسُوا مِنْ رَحْمَتِي ، فلزم الفريقين اسم الكفر والخلود في النار . وأما المؤمنون بآيات الله وصفوه عفوا غفورا رحيما محققين لذلك ، فهم لهم الرجاء ، ولا يجوز لهم الشهادة بواحد من الأمرين ، فتولى كل قول كما قال الله تعالى : نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى وَنُصْلِهِ إلا بالله . والثانى أنهم جميعا ضيقوا رحمة الله فجعلوها بحيث لا تتسع لذنب؛ إذ الذنوب التي ليست بكبائر لا يجوز معها التغذيب ، فليس لرحمة الله فيما ليس له التعذيب : ولا لعشوه فيما استغنى عنه بالحكمة ، وجعلوا الغضب والسخط كل ذنب في الحكمة يجوز له التعليب ، فلا عفو إذا على قولهم ولا رحمة ، فحق هذا القول الحرمان . وأما من يصفه بسعة الرحمة وعظيم العفو فحق له المغفرة والعفو ؛ لأن كل كريم يوصف بهذا ، فهو أميل له من الوصف له بما وصفته الخوارج والمعتزلة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والثالث قال الله تعالى : إِنْ يَنْتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُمْ مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ ، ولا يجوز أن يكون الذي به الانتهاء غير محدود ولا معروف الوصول إلى جميع الطاعات والقيام بجميع الأمور بتأخر الحياة على قول الخوارج فتصير بحيث لا انتهاء عنه ، وكذلك على قول المعتزلة ، فثبت أن الانتهاء هو الذى يملكه كله في كل وقت ، وهو البرء عن كل أنواع الكفر والمعاصى ، والإيمان بالله تعالى وبجميع ما يؤمن المرء به ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وهذا على قول المعتزلة إذ جعلوا بين الكفر والإيمان منزلة ، والله تعالى وعد ما ذكر بالإنتهاء عن الكفر ، يلزم أن يكون صاحب الكبيرة مغفورا له ، وخاصة الكافر إذ كان مع الانتهاء من الكفر مرتكب الكبائر ، فيجب بالذي ادعى من العموم فى التخليد دفع العذاب والمغفرة ، والله والموفق .
Their saying: [in] the Book of Tawhid, they are deserving of eternity in the Fire, and others among the sects claiming Islam [refuted] by aspects: one of them that they agreed upon [that] whom God has mercy... and that is the description of disbelief with what was mentioned from the verse and by His saying: 'And those who disbelieve in the signs of God and meeting Him, those despair of My mercy' so the name of disbelief and eternity in the Fire became binding upon both groups. As for those who believe in the signs of God, they describe Him as forgiving, pardoning, merciful, confirming that, so they have hope, and it is not permissible for them to testify to one of the two matters, so every saying is undertaken as God said: 'We will assign him what he has chosen and roast him [in Hell]?' except by God. The second: that they all restricted the mercy of God, making it such that it does not encompass sin; since sins that are not major are not permissible to punish with, so there is no mercy of God in what punishment is not for, nor [?] what is independent of wisdom, and they made anger and wrath every sin in wisdom permissible for punishment, so there is no pardon on their saying and no mercy, so this saying deserves deprivation. As for one who describes Him with vast mercy and great pardon, then forgiveness and pardon are his due; because every generous one described with this is more inclined to it than to the description with which the Khawarij and Mu'tazila described Him, and there is no power except with God. The third: God said: 'If they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them,' and it is not possible that the one by whom desisting occurs is unlimited nor known to reach all acts of obedience and undertaking all matters with delay of life according to the Khawarij, so it becomes such that there is no desisting from it, and likewise according to the Mu'tazila, so it is established that desisting is one who possesses all of it at every time, and it is turning away from all types of disbelief and sins, and faith in God Almighty and all that one believes in, and there is no power except with God. This is according to the Mu'tazila since they made a station between disbelief and faith, and God promised what was mentioned regarding desisting from disbelief, it necessitates that the committer of a major sin is forgiven, especially the disbeliever since while desisting from disbelief he commits major sins, so by what he claimed of universality in eternity, the repulsion of punishment and forgiveness is necessary, and God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 934

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments (أوجه) refuting the positions of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila regarding eternal punishment and God's mercy. The first argument (أحدها) states that both groups agree on describing disbelief with a verse (Quran 29:23) that mentions despair of mercy, so the name of disbelief and eternity in fire applies to both. The second argument (والثاني) accuses both of restricting God's mercy, arguing that if mercy does not encompass sin, then there is no forgiveness, but God is described as vast mercy and pardon. The third argument (والثالث) uses Quran 8:38 to show that desisting from disbelief leads to forgiveness, and since according to Khawarij and Mu'tazila desisting is impossible or undefined, it is established that true desisting is complete repentance and faith. The passage then concludes that on the Mu'tazilite view of a station between faith and disbelief, the committer of a major sin must be forgiven, refuting their claim of universal eternity.

Key Terms
الخلود
السخط
الغضب
الانتهاء
الكبيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Maturidi agrees with the Khawarij and Mu'tazila that major sinners deserve eternal punishment.
Correction: Maturidi explicitly refutes them, arguing that God's mercy is vast and that true repentance (even after a lifetime of sin) leads to forgiveness, and that their own logic leads to contradictions.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's third argument, what is the true meaning of 'desisting' (الانتهاء)?
A) Merely ceasing a particular sin
B) Complete repentance from all disbelief and sins and having faith
C) A temporary state that may be lost
D) An outward act without inner faith

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's three arguments collectively demonstrate that eternal punishment is reserved for disbelief, not for major sins, because God's mercy encompasses all and true repentance is always possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own sins, do you truly believe God's mercy is vast enough to forgive them, or do you secretly doubt? What would it take to have that certainty?
?
The Khawarij and Mu'tazila restricted God's mercy. Where in your own life have you restricted God's mercy—by thinking some sin is too great, or some person beyond forgiveness? Will you repent of that?
?
Maturidi argues that true 'desisting' includes complete repentance and faith. Are you holding back any part of your life from turning to God? What would it mean for you to fully desist from a specific sin today?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Position: First Two Options
Maturidi refutes the first two options of the Mu'tazilite position on naming the grave sinner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite position on the grave sinner and Maturidi's refutation of their first two logical options.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilite 'middle position' on the grave sinner collapses into absurdity when logically examined.

Maturidi begins by stating the Mu'tazilite claim that the grave sinner should not be called a believer or a disbeliever. He then presents them with three possible interpretations of their stance and refutes each. In this lesson, we explore the first two options and their logical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite position
Read the opening sentence where Maturidi quotes the Mu'tazilite claim that the grave sinner has no name of faith or disbelief.
This sets up the refutation.
2
Understand the first option and its refutation
Examine the first option: that the sinner has no name at all. Follow Maturidi's question: has he come with all, some, or no faith? See how each leads to a contradiction.
If he has all faith, denying him the name 'believer' is absurd; if some faith, the Quran calls such people disbelievers.
3
Understand the second option and its refutation
Look at the second option: that the sinner has a mixture of faith and disbelief. Maturidi refutes this by citing God's condemnation of those who believe in part and disbelieve in part, showing that they are called disbelievers.
This is the view of the Khawarij.
4
See the logical consequences
Reflect on how both options force the Mu'tazila into either absurdity or the Kharijite position, showing their stance is untenable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسم فعليه تقد للمعتزلة : قولكم : لا يسمى صاحب الكبيرة باسم الإيمان ولا باسم الكفر ، ولا يسمونه بما لا يستحق واحدا من الاسمين أو له أحدهما ، ولا تعلمونه أنتم ، فإن قالوا بالأول فيقال لهم : أو قد أتى هو بكل الإيمان أو بعضه أو لم يأت بشي . ؟ لذلك بطل اسمه ، فان قال بالأول أعظم القول ومنع عنه وقد أتى به وجهل بريه حيث لم يحقق ما له اسمه ، ولو جاز ذا الجاز أن لا يكون أحد جاء بالصدق، عند الله فى الحقيقة صادقا ، وكذلك قائم وقاعد وذو حال لا يجوز معنا الله كذلك ، أو الله يعلمه كذلك ، وعلى ذلك مضادات التي ذكرنا ، وهذا آية جهلهم بالله, وإن قال بالثاني فقد شهد الله للذين آمنوا ببعض وكفروا ببعض بأن قالوا : نؤمن ببعض وتكفر ببعض ، كفارا حقا لزمهم التسمية بذلك ، وهو رأى الخوارج. وإن قالوا بالثالث فهو أبعد ؛ إذ الله تعالى سمى المؤمن ببعض كافرا ، فمن ليس معه شيء أحق بذلك . وأيَّد هذا الأصل وجهان : أحدهما ما ذكرت من قسم الله البشر قسمين فى أمر الدنيا والآخرة ، فقسمة المعتزلة على ثلاثة أقسام تعدى لحد الله ، وحق مثله أن يقال له : الله أذن لكم أم على الله تفترون ، أو يقال أأنتم أعلم أم الله كما قيل لليهود . والثاني أن الله تعالى نفى الإيمان في محكم تنزيله عن قوم على تحقيق الكفر إذ قال : " وَمَا أُولَئِكَ بِالمُؤْمِنِينَ ، ولم يخطر ببال عاقل أنهم لعلهم ليسوا بكفار ، بل إذا أزيل الإيمان عمن يكون له فعل الإيمان فإنما يزال بالكفر ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وإن قالوا لا يعلم له أجد الإسمين، وله ذلك عند الله كفوا مؤونه الجدل؛ لأن ما لا يعلمونه أكثر مما يحصى ، لو لزم محاجتهم فيها ليذهب العمر باطلا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
A name upon it? Presented to the Mu'tazila: Your statement: you do not call the committer of a major sin by the name of faith nor by the name of disbelief, and you do not name him with something that does not deserve one of the two names or he has one of them, and you do not know it yourselves. If they say by the first, then it is said to them: Has he come with all of faith or some of it or did he not come with anything? Therefore his name becomes invalid. If he says by the first, he magnifies the statement and prevents it while he has come with it, and he is ignorant of his innocence? where he did not realize what his name is. If this were permissible, it would be permissible that one who comes with truth, according to God in reality, is not truthful, and likewise standing and sitting and one in a state, it is not permissible with us that God is likewise, or God knows him likewise, and upon that are the opposites we mentioned, and this is a sign of their ignorance of God. If he says by the second, then God has testified for those who believe in some and disbelieve in some, that they said: 'We believe in some and disbelieve in some,' [they are] true disbelievers, so naming by that becomes binding on them, and it is the view of the Khawarij. If they say by the third, it is more remote; since God called one who believes in some a disbeliever, so one who has nothing with him is more deserving of that. This principle is supported by two aspects: one of them is what I mentioned of God dividing people into two divisions in the matter of this world and the Hereafter; the Mu'tazila's division into three divisions is a transgression of God's limit, and it is fitting that one says to him: 'Did God permit you or do you invent lies against God?' or 'Are you more knowing or is God?' as was said to the Jews. The second: that God negated faith in His clear revelation from a people while affirming disbelief when He said: 'And those are not believers,' and it did not occur to any intelligent person that perhaps they are not disbelievers. Rather, if faith is removed from one who has the act of faith, it is only removed by disbelief. And there is no power except with God. If they say they do not know for him one of the two names, and he has that with God, they spare themselves the trouble of argument; because what they do not know is more than can be counted; if argument with them about it were necessary, life would be wasted in vain. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 935

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite position that the grave sinner (صاحب الكبيرة) should neither be called a believer nor a disbeliever. Maturidi presents a series of logical objections. If they say the sinner has no name, then he must have brought all of faith, some of it, or none; if all, then he is a believer, if some, then Scripture calls such people disbelievers (like those who believe in part and disbelieve in part), which is the Kharijite view. If they claim they do not know, they are ignorant. The principle is supported by two aspects: (1) God divides people into two groups, not three, and the Mu'tazilite threefold division transgresses God's limit; (2) God in the Quran negates faith from people while affirming they are disbelievers, so if faith is removed, it is replaced by disbelief. Finally, if they plead ignorance, they avoid argument but that is no excuse.

Key Terms
صاحب الكبيرة
الإيمان
الكفر
التسمية
المنزلة بين المنزلتين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite claim that the grave sinner is in a middle state between faith and disbelief is a valid and coherent position.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this position leads to absurdity if the sinner has all faith, or to the Kharijite view of takfir if he has some faith. The Quran does not recognize a third category.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the Quran call those who believe in some parts and disbelieve in others?
A) True believers
B) True disbelievers
C) Neither believers nor disbelievers
D) Hypocrites

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazilite claim by showing that their stance implies either absurd logical consequences or the Kharijite view of takfir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a fellow Muslim who commits a major sin, do you find yourself mentally distancing them from the faith? How does Maturidi's insistence on logical consistency force you to examine the criteria you use to judge others' iman?
?
Are you ever tempted to adopt a 'middle ground' in matters of faith to avoid conflict, even if that position contradicts the clear rulings of the Quran? What would it cost you to uphold the truth as Maturidi does, even when it is uncomfortable?

The Third Option and the Quranic Division
Maturidi refutes the third option and provides two Quranic principles to support the twofold division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the third Mu'tazilite option and his two supporting principles from the Quran.

Core Idea
God's division of humanity into believers and disbelievers leaves no room for a middle category.

In the final part of his refutation, Maturidi addresses the third possible interpretation—that we don't know the sinner's name. He then provides two principles from the Quran to support his own position, emphasizing that God divides people into two groups, not three.

Guided Path
1
Understand the third option and its refutation
Read Maturidi's dismissal of the Mu'tazilite claim that the grave sinner's name is unknown. Note his reasoning: since God already calls those with partial belief disbelievers, one with no faith is even more deserving.
This third option is even weaker than the first two.
2
Analyze the first principle: God's twofold division
Examine the first principle (wajh): God divides people into two groups in both worldly and religious matters. The Mu'tazilite threefold division transgresses God's limit.
The proper response is to ask whether God permitted this or if they invent lies against Him.
3
Analyze the second principle: negation of faith implies disbelief
Look at the second principle: when God negates faith from a people, it confirms that they are disbelievers (e.g., Quran 2:8). No sensible person would think otherwise.
Removal of faith implies disbelief; there is no intermediate state.
4
Consider the final response about ignorance
Read Maturidi's conclusion that pleading ignorance does not resolve the issue; it only avoids argument. The Quranic division remains clear.

Maturidi on the Intermediate Status Refutation
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila claim of an intermediate status for grave sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument against the Mu'tazila doctrine of an intermediate status for grave sinners and why God's promise of forgiveness overrides the claim of eternal punishment.

Core Idea
God's promise of forgiveness overrules the Mu'tazila's intermediate status.

In this lesson, we examine Maturidi's concise refutation of the Mu'tazila claim that a grave sinner occupies a station between faith and disbelief. Maturidi invokes God's promise of forgiveness for those who refrain from disbelief to show that such sinners must be forgiven, not punished eternally.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note the structure: Maturidi begins by stating the Mu'tazila position, then presents his logical deduction.
2
Identify the key elements
Find the Mu'tazila claim (intermediate station) and Maturidi's premise (God's promise to those who refrain from disbelief). Notice how he connects them with 'yalzam' (it necessarily follows).
The phrase 'يلزم أن يكون' signals a logical necessity.
3
Understand the logical argument
Maturidi argues: Since the grave sinner refrains from disbelief (by not being a disbeliever), God's promise of forgiveness applies. Therefore, the Mu'tazila cannot claim eternal punishment for such a person.
This refutes the Mu'tazila's position by showing their own premise leads to the opposite conclusion.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this argument upholds the mainstream Sunni view that grave sinners are still believers and may be forgiven, as long as they do not commit disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا على قول المعتزلة إذ جعلوا بين الكفر والإيمان منزلة ، والله تعالى وعد ما ذكر بالإنتهاء عن الكفر ، يلزم أن يكون صاحب الكبيرة مغفورا له ، وخاصة الكافر إذ كان مع الانتهاء من الكفر مرتكب الكبائر ، فيجب بالذي ادعى من العموم فى التخليد دفع العذاب والمغفرة ، والله الموفق.
This is according to the statement of the Mu'tazila when they placed a station between disbelief and faith. And God Almighty promised what was mentioned regarding refraining from disbelief. It necessarily follows that the committer of a grave sin is forgiven, especially the disbeliever since, while refraining from disbelief, he commits grave sins. So by what he claimed of generality in eternal punishment, it is necessary to repel punishment and grant forgiveness. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 935

Commentary
This passage presents Maturidi's initial refutation of the Mu'tazila doctrine of al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn (the intermediate station). The Mu'tazila claim that a grave sinner (sahib al-kabira) is neither a believer nor a disbeliever but in an intermediate position. Maturidi argues that God has promised forgiveness to those who refrain from disbelief (kufr). Therefore, if a person refrains from disbelief, even if he commits grave sins, God's promise necessitates forgiveness. This applies especially to the disbeliever who, upon refraining from disbelief, commits grave sins. Thus, the Mu'tazila claim of eternal punishment for such a person is invalid, as forgiveness is required by God's promise. Maturidi concludes by saying 'wa-Allah al-muwaffiq' (And God is the grantor of success).

Key Terms
مرتكب الكبائر (committer of grave sins)
المنزلة بين المنزلتين (intermediate station)
الخلود (eternal punishment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Grave sinners deserve eternal punishment because they are in an intermediate state between faith and disbelief.
Correction: Maturidi shows that if they refrain from disbelief, God's promise of forgiveness applies, so they cannot be eternally punished.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the necessary consequence of the Mu'tazila's claim that a grave sinner is in an intermediate station?
A) The grave sinner deserves eternal punishment.
B) The grave sinner is a believer.
C) The grave sinner must be forgiven because God promised forgiveness to those who refrain from disbelief.
D) The grave sinner has no religious status.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila intermediate status by showing that God's promise of forgiveness to those who refrain from disbelief logically requires forgiveness for the grave sinner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a grave sin, do you truly believe that God's promise of forgiveness applies to you because you refrain from disbelief? Or do you secretly fear that you are in an intermediate state, neither fully forgiven nor condemned? How does Maturidi's argument challenge you to have true reliance on God's mercy while still struggling against sin?
?
The Mu'tazila say that a grave sinner is eternally punished unless they repent. Does your own view of your sins sometimes mirror this harshness? How would your daily life change if you fully accepted that, because you have faith (refrain from disbelief), you are already forgiven by God's promise, and that this forgiveness should inspire you to avoid sin out of gratitude, not fear?

Refutation of Mu'tazila on Naming the Grave Sinner
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila by examining three logical possibilities and providing two scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the grave sinner must be called either a believer or a disbeliever, and why any intermediate category contradicts divine classification.

Core Idea
The grave sinner cannot be an intermediate; he is either a believer or a disbeliever based on the Quranic dichotomy.

The Mu'tazila proposed a 'middle ground' for grave sinners, neither believer nor disbeliever. In this passage, Imam Maturidi systematically dismantles that position by examining the logical possibilities and appealing to Quranic proofs. You will see how he forces the Mu'tazila into either the Khawarij view or an even more extreme position, ultimately showing that only a binary classification is consistent with revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila statement and Maturidi's opening question
Understand the three logical possibilities Maturidi poses: the sinner has performed all faith, some faith, or none.
Maturidi begins by presenting the Mu'tazila claim that the grave sinner is not called believer or disbeliever.
2
Follow Maturidi's refutation of each possibility
For each possibility, Maturidi shows it leads to contradiction or an undesirable conclusion: (a) if all faith, then sin contradicts; (b) if some faith, leads to Khawarij view; (c) if none, even more deserving of disbelief.
3
Examine the two supporting arguments
Maturidi supports his reasoning with: (1) God divides people into two groups (believers and disbelievers) in this world and the Hereafter, so a third division transgresses His limit; (2) God negated faith from some while confirming their disbelief (Quran 2:8-9).
These arguments show that the intermediate state is impossible.
4
Consider the final point about Mu'tazila claiming ignorance
If the Mu'tazila admit they do not know which name the sinner deserves, then they should not argue, as they are ignorant of many things.
This undermines their entire position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقد للمعتزلة : قولكم : لا يسمى صاحب الكبيرة باسم الإيمان ولا باسم الكفر ، ولا يسمونه بما لا يستحق واحدا من الاسمين أو له أحدهما ، ولا تعلمونه أنتم ، فإن قالوا بالأول فيقال لهم : أو قد أتى هو بكل الإيمان أو بعضه أو لم يأت بشي . ؟ لذلك بطل اسمه ، فان قال بالأول أعظم القول ومنع عنه وقد أتى به وجهل بريه حيث لم يحقق ما له اسمه ، ولو جاز ذا الجاز أن لا يكون أحد جاء بالصدق، عند الله فى الحقيقة صادقا ، وكذلك قائم وقاعد وذو حال لا يجوز معنا الله كذلك ، أو الله يعلمه كذلك ، وعلى ذلك مضادات التي ذكرنا ، وهذا آية جهلهم بالله, وإن قال بالثاني فقد شهد الله للذين آمنوا ببعض وكفروا ببعض بأن قالوا : نؤمن ببعض وتكفر ببعض ، كفارا حقا لزمهم التسمية بذلك ، وهو رأى الخوارج. وإن قالوا بالثالث فهو أبعد ؛ إذ الله تعالى سمى المؤمن ببعض كافرا ، فمن ليس معه شيء أحق بذلك . وأيد هذا الأصل وجهان : أحدهما ما ١٧٠ ذكرت من قسم الله البشر قسمين فى أمر الدنيا والآخرة ، فقسمة المعتزلة على ثلاثة أقسام تعدى لحد الله ، وحق مثله أن يقال له : الله أذن لكم أم على الله تفترون ، أو يقال أأنتم أعلم أم الله كما قيل لليهود . والثاني أن الله تعالى نفى الإيمان في محكم تنزيله عن قوم على تحقيق الكفر إذ قال : " وَمَا أُولَئِكَ بِالمُؤْمِنِينَ ، ولم يخطر ببال عاقل أنهم لعلهم ليسوا بكفار ، بل إذا أزيل الإيمان ـ عمن يكون له فعل الإيمان" - فإنما يزال بالكفر ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وإن قالوا لا يعلم له أجد الإسمين، وله ذلك عند الله كفوا مؤونه الجدل؛ لأن ما لا يعلمونه أكثر مما يحصى ، لو لزم محاجتهم فيها ليذهب العمر باطلا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Present to the Mu'tazila: Your statement: 'The committer of a grave sin is not called by the name of faith nor by the name of disbelief, and they do not name him with what does not deserve one of the two names, or he has one of them, and you do not know it.' If they say the first, then it is said to them: 'Has he performed all of faith, or some of it, or not performed anything?' Therefore his name is invalid. If he says the first, he makes the statement great and prevents it while he has performed it, and he is ignorant of his opinion because he did not verify what his name is. If this were allowed, it would be allowed that someone who brings truth is not in reality truthful in God's sight, and likewise standing, sitting, and a state of being; it is not permitted with God likewise, or God knows him likewise. And this is a sign of their ignorance of God. If he says the second, God has testified for those who believe in some and disbelieve in some, when they say: 'We believe in some and disbelieve in some,' that they are true disbelievers. Necessarily they are named with that, and that is the opinion of the Khawarij. If they say the third, it is even more remote, for God Almighty named one who believes in some a disbeliever, so one who has nothing is more deserving of that. This principle is supported by two aspects: one of them is what I mentioned about God dividing people into two divisions in the matter of this world and the Hereafter. The division of the Mu'tazila into three divisions exceeds God's limit, and the like of him deserves that it be said to him: 'Did God permit you, or do you invent lies against God?' Or it is said: 'Are you more knowledgeable or is God?' as was said to the Jews. The second is that God Almighty negated faith in the clear revelation from people while confirming disbelief when He said: 'And those are not the believers.' It never occurs to a sane person that perhaps they are not disbelievers. Rather, when faith is removed from one who has the act of faith, it is removed only by disbelief. And there is no power except with God. And if they say they do not know which of the two names is due to him, and that is with God, then they have been spared the trouble of argument. For what they do not know is more than can be counted; if disputation with them were necessary, life would be wasted in vain. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 935

Commentary
This passage contains Maturidi's detailed refutation of the Mu'tazila position on naming the grave sinner. He presents their statement that the grave sinner is not called a believer or a disbeliever, and they do not know which name he deserves. Maturidi examines three logical possibilities: (1) the sinner has performed all of faith, (2) some of faith, or (3) none. If they say the first (he performed all faith), then that contradicts his sin. If they say the second (he performed some faith), then God has declared such people (those who believe partially) as disbelievers, like the Khawarij view. If they say the third (he performed none), then he is even more deserving of being called a disbeliever. Maturidi supports this reasoning with two arguments: First, God divides people into two categories (believers and disbelievers) in this world and the Hereafter, so the Mu'tazila's three-part division transgresses God's limits. They should be asked whether God permitted this or they invent lies. Second, God negated faith from a people while confirming their disbelief (Quran 2:8-9), showing that removing faith necessarily means disbelief, not an intermediate state. Finally, Maturidi notes that if the Mu'tazila admit ignorance of the sinner's true name, then they should not argue, as they are ignorant of many things.

Key Terms
صاحب الكبيرة (committer of a grave sin)
الإيمان (faith)
الكفر (disbelief)
الخوارج (Khawarij)
تعدى حد الله (transgressing God's limit)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila position (grave sinner is neither believer nor disbeliever) is a rationally consistent middle ground.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the position either leads to the Khawarij view (if the sinner has some faith) or an even more extreme view (if no faith), and it contradicts the Quranic binary classification.

Checkpoint
Which group's opinion does Maturidi say is similar to the second possibility (believing in some and disbelieving in some)?
A) The Mu'tazila
B) The Khawarij
C) The Ash'aris
D) The Jews

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the only consistent Quranic position is a binary classification of believers and disbelievers, with no intermediate category for grave sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you currently commit a major sin and still call yourself a believer, is your faith truly intact? What would it take for you to lose your faith entirely? Examine your heart: is there any area where you 'believe in some and disbelieve in some'?
?
Maturidi says God negates faith from hypocrites and confirms their disbelief. Could you be unknowingly in that category if you persist in sin without repentance? What concrete step will you take today to ensure your faith is genuine?
?
The lesson shows that there is no middle ground: you are either a believer or a disbeliever. Does your daily life reflect that you are firmly on the side of faith, or have you been complacent, assuming a 'neutral' status? What will you change to align your actions with your claim of faith?

The Umma's Consensus on the Grave Sinner's Name
Maturidi asserts the umma's consensus on naming the grave sinner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the Muslim community unanimously agrees that the grave sinner has one of three religious names (shirk, kufr, or Islam), and that denying this consensus is a nullification of agreed-upon truth.

Core Idea
The grave sinner's religious name is not optional; the umma has agreed on it.

Maturidi opens by appealing to the collective agreement (ijma) of the entire Muslim community, despite their internal disagreements, on a foundational point: every grave sinner has a religious designation. This consensus, he argues, is not merely academic but is grounded in the Qur'an and Sunnah. Those who reject it out of fear of uncertainty have actually rejected what the community has affirmed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on consensus
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Focus on Maturidi's claim that the community agreed that the grave sinner has a name from the religions (shirk, kufr, or Islam).
Notice the use of 'then' (ثم) to continue the argument.
2
Identify the consensus and its basis
Maturidi says the consensus is affirmed by the Book and Sunnah. Reflect on why he emphasizes testimony of the Book and Sunnah.
He also mentions that doubt is removed for those who listen sincerely.
3
Consider the warning against nullification
Maturidi warns that whoever nullifies these names out of caution against doubt has nullified what the community agreed upon. Think about the nature of this warning.
What does it imply about the gravity of rejecting consensus?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأمة على اختلافهم اتفقت على أن لصاحب الكبيرة اسما من الأديان من شرك أو كفر أو إسلام ، فمن أبطلها توقيا أن ينطق بالشك أبطل ما أجمع على القول به ، وشهدوا على مجيء الكتاب به والسنة بما لديه يرتفع الريب عمن تلقى السمع وهو شهيد أو له قلب ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم القول بالفاسق والفاجر مطلقا مما يتوزع فيه ، ومن سماه كافرا أو مشركا أطلقه ، ومن سماه مؤمنا أبى ذلك ، وكذلك جحدوا اسم أعداء الله ، وأبدعت المعتزلة هذين الاسمين على منع ذينك الاسمين خلافا لما عليه الأمر ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
Then the community, despite their differences, agreed that for the committer of a grave sin there is a name from the religions: either shirk, or disbelief, or Islam. So whoever nullifies them, out of caution against uttering doubt, has nullified what the community agreed to affirm. And they testified that the Book and the Sunnah have brought [these names]. With what he has, doubt is removed from one who receives hearing while being a witness or has a heart. And there is no power except with God. Then the statement 'fasiq' (immoral) and 'fajir' (sinner) absolutely is something subject to division. Whoever names him a disbeliever or polytheist applies [that name]; whoever names him a believer refuses that. And likewise they denied the name 'enemies of God.' The Mu'tazila innovated these two names (fasiq and fajir) to prevent those two names (disbeliever and polytheist), contrary to the actual state of affairs. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 936

Commentary
This passage begins by asserting that the entire Muslim community (umma) agrees, despite their differences, that the grave sinner has a specific religious name: either polytheism (shirk), disbelief (kufr), or Islam. Whoever denies this naming, out of fear of falling into doubt (shakk), has actually denied what the community has agreed upon. The community testifies that the Quran and Sunnah have brought these names. Those who listen sincerely and have a heart will have doubt removed. Then Maturidi discusses the terms 'fasiq' and 'fajir'. Some apply these names absolutely to the grave sinner, while others reserve them. Those who call him 'disbeliever' or 'polytheist' apply the term absolutely; those who call him 'believer' refuse that label. The Mu'tazila have innovated these two names ('fasiq' and 'fajir') as a middle ground, to avoid calling him either disbeliever or believer, which contradicts the actual state of affairs. Maturidi emphasizes that this innovation goes against the consensus and the clear texts.

Key Terms
إجماع الأمة (consensus of the community)
صاحب الكبيرة (committer of a grave sin)
شك (doubt)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think it is safer to avoid naming the grave sinner at all, to avoid making a judgment.
Correction: Maturidi says this avoidance actually nullifies the agreed truth brought by revelation; the umma has affirmed that a name exists.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what did the umma agree on regarding the grave sinner?
A) That he has no religious name.
B) That he has a name from the religions: shirk, kufr, or Islam.
C) That he is to be called only 'fasiq' or 'fajir'.
D) That his name depends on the scholar's opinion.

Key Takeaway
The Muslim community has always agreed that every grave sinner has a religious name from revelation, and denying this is a serious innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you immediately try to avoid labeling them out of a false sense of safety? How does Maturidi’s warning against nullifying consensus shake your excuse?
?
The umma has agreed that a grave sinner has a religious name — yet your heart may still prefer to blur the line. Are you willing to submit to the community’s consensus even when it is uncomfortable? What name would you now give that person, and why?
?
The passage ends with ‘There is no power except with God.’ How does your dependence on Allah challenge your fear of misjudging others? Will you trust His guidance in the Book and Sunnah more than your own caution?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on Fasiq and Fajir
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila innovation of fasiq/fajir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of the Mu'tazila for inventing the names 'fasiq' and 'fajir' for the grave sinner, and how this innovation contradicts the consensus and the clear names from revelation.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila's middle-ground names are an innovation against the agreed religious names.

After establishing the consensus on religious names for the grave sinner, Maturidi turns to the Mu'tazila position. They introduced the terms 'fasiq' (immoral) and 'fajir' (sinner) as a middle ground, avoiding both 'disbeliever' and 'believer'. Maturidi argues that this is a bid'a (innovation) that contradicts the actual state of affairs and the consensus of the umma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on fasiq/fajir
Carefully read the Arabic and translation, noting how Maturidi describes the division over these terms and directly criticizes the Mu'tazila.
Look for the contrast between 'those who call him disbeliever' and 'those who call him believer'.
2
Analyze the innovation claim
Maturidi says the Mu'tazila innovated (أبدعت) the two names to prevent applying the names from revelation. Reflect on why he considers this a bid'a.
Consider how this relates to the earlier consensus.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi ends with 'there is no power except with God', emphasizing that the truth is from God alone. Ask yourself what the 'actual state of affairs' is that the Mu'tazila contradicted.
The actual state is that the grave sinner is either a disbeliever or a believer, not a third category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأمة على اختلافهم اتفقت على أن لصاحب الكبيرة اسما من الأديان من شرك أو كفر أو إسلام ، فمن أبطلها توقيا أن ينطق بالشك أبطل ما أجمع على القول به ، وشهدوا على مجيء الكتاب به والسنة بما لديه يرتفع الريب عمن تلقى السمع وهو شهيد أو له قلب ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم القول بالفاسق والفاجر مطلقا مما يتوزع فيه ، ومن سماه كافرا أو مشركا أطلقه ، ومن سماه مؤمنا أبى ذلك ، وكذلك جحدوا اسم أعداء الله ، وأبدعت المعتزلة هذين الاسمين على منع ذينك الاسمين خلافا لما عليه الأمر ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
Then the community, despite their differences, agreed that for the committer of a grave sin there is a name from the religions: either shirk, or disbelief, or Islam. So whoever nullifies them, out of caution against uttering doubt, has nullified what the community agreed to affirm. And they testified that the Book and the Sunnah have brought [these names]. With what he has, doubt is removed from one who receives hearing while being a witness or has a heart. And there is no power except with God. Then the statement 'fasiq' (immoral) and 'fajir' (sinner) absolutely is something subject to division. Whoever names him a disbeliever or polytheist applies [that name]; whoever names him a believer refuses that. And likewise they denied the name 'enemies of God.' The Mu'tazila innovated these two names (fasiq and fajir) to prevent those two names (disbeliever and polytheist), contrary to the actual state of affairs. And there is no power except with God.

Commentary
This passage begins by asserting that the entire Muslim community (umma) agrees, despite their differences, that the grave sinner has a specific religious name: either polytheism (shirk), disbelief (kufr), or Islam. Whoever denies this naming, out of fear of falling into doubt (shakk), has actually denied what the community has agreed upon. The community testifies that the Quran and Sunnah have brought these names. Those who listen sincerely and have a heart will have doubt removed. Then Maturidi discusses the terms 'fasiq' and 'fajir'. Some apply these names absolutely to the grave sinner, while others reserve them. Those who call him 'disbeliever' or 'polytheist' apply the term absolutely; those who call him 'believer' refuse that label. Key Terms
فاسق (immoral)
فاجر (sinner)
بدعة (innovation)
المعتزلة (the Mu'tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the terms 'fasiq' and 'fajir' are a legitimate neutral category for the grave sinner.
Correction: Maturidi argues these terms are an innovation that violates the consensus and the revealed names; the grave sinner is either a believer or a disbeliever.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why did the Mu'tazila innovate the names 'fasiq' and 'fajir'?
A) To follow the consensus of the umma.
B) To prevent using the names 'disbeliever' and 'polytheist'.
C) To describe the grave sinner's moral state accurately.
D) To honor the grave sinner by giving him a better name.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's introduction of fasiq/fajir is an innovation aimed at avoiding the revealed names, and it contradicts the reality and consensus of the umma.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a label for yourself or others that you knew was not from the Quran or Sunnah, just to avoid a harsher truth? What was that label, and what would it mean to replace it with a revealed name? Are you ready to do that today?
?
When you hear someone call a fellow Muslim 'fasiq' or 'fajir', do you accept that term without questioning whether it comes from revelation or from human innovation? How will you check every label you use against the Book and Sunnah from now on?
?
The Mu'tazila introduced their names with the best of intentions—to find a middle path. But Maturidi calls it an innovation. Is there a 'middle path' in your life that you have invented to avoid a clear command of Allah? What is it, and what step can you take today to abandon it?

Refuting Khawarij on Verse 4:48
Maturidi refutes Khawarij on verse 4:48.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi rejects the Khawarij interpretation of 'Allah does not forgive shirk' and how the verse distinguishes between shirk and other sins.

Core Idea
The verse on shirk is about distinction, not requiring repentance for forgiveness.

The Khawarij claimed that verse 4:48 implies that only shirk is unforgivable without repentance, but Maturidi argues this is a corrupt interpretation. He explains that the verse simply distinguishes between shirk and other sins, not that repentance is needed for forgiveness. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on verse 4:48
Read the Arabic and translation for Maturidi's refutation of the Khawarij interpretation of 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him.'
Pay attention to why he says the Khawarij interpretation is 'corrupt error'.
2
Understand the distinction
Maturidi says the verse 'does not permit the implication of repentance' and that it 'distinguishes between the two sins.' Ask: why does he say this?
The Khawarij thought the verse proves that all sins except shirk can be forgiven if repented, but Maturidi sees it as a categorical distinction.
3
Reflect on the key point
Consider that Maturidi is not denying that repentance is necessary for forgiveness in general, but rather that this particular verse is about the distinction between shirk and other sins, not about the conditions for forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قوله : إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ ، تأويل الخوارج فيه من الخطأ فاسد ؛ لأنه ليس بذنب فيغفر ، وفى هذا ذكر المغفرة ، ولا يحتمل إضمار التوبة لما يغفر بمثله الشرك ، والآية فى التمييز بين الذنبين ، وكذلك لا يحتمل قوله : إِن تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ ، ؛ لما فيه التكفير ، وما لا ذنب لا يكفر والخطأ لا يحقق الذنب ، والتكفير يكون لشيء يجز به ، ولا يحتمل ما قالت المعتزلة لأن قولهم يمنع تحقيق الشبه ؛ إذ هي تقع من مجتنب الكبائر [١١٧٦] مغفورة ، وفى هذا اثباتها ، ثم التكفير ، وهم يجعلونها مغفور [٠] لا مكفرة ؛ إذ المغفورة هى التى تستر عليها ، وفى بقائها إلى مدة دفعها ، والمكفره هي التي يأتى من صاحبها فعل حسن يكفر به نحو قوله : " فَأُولَئِكَ يُبَدِّلُ اللهُ سَيِّئَاتِهِم حَسَنَاتٍ ، ٥ ، وقوله : هَلْ أَدُلُّكُمْ عَلَى تِجَارَةٍ ، وقوله : ( إِنْ تُبْدُوا الصَّدَقَاتِ ،
Then His statement: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him' (4:48). The interpretation of the Khawarij regarding it is corrupt error, because it is not a sin that is forgiven. And in this mention of forgiveness, it does not permit the implication of repentance, for that by which shirk is forgiven is similar to it. And the verse distinguishes between the two sins. Likewise, His statement: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden' (4:31) does not permit [their interpretation], because of the expiation (takfir) it contains. And that which is not a sin does not expiate, and error does not confirm sin. Expiation is for something by which one is recompensed. And that which the Mu'tazila said is not permissible, because their statement prevents the confirmation of the ambiguities, since they occur from one who avoids major sins and is forgiven. And in this is affirmation of them, then expiation. They make them forgiven, not expiated. For the forgiven is that which is concealed, and its remaining until the time of its removal. And the expiated is that for which the doer performs a good deed that expiates it, similar to His statement: 'Those, Allah will replace their evil deeds with good deeds' (25:70), and His statement: 'Shall I guide you to a transaction?' (61:10), and His statement: 'If you give alms openly' (2:271).
Source pages p. 936

Commentary
This passage focuses on the interpretation of Quranic verses related to forgiveness and expiation, refuting both the Khawarij and the Mu'tazila. Maturidi first discusses verse 4:48 ('Allah does not forgive shirk'). He says the Khawarij interpretation is corrupt because the verse is about distinguishing between shirk and other sins, not about requiring repentance for forgiveness. The verse mentions forgiveness directly, so implying repentance (tawba) is not permissible here. Similarly, verse 4:31 (avoid major sins) does not require repentance; it speaks of expiation (takfir) of minor sins. Expiation (takfir) is for something that recompenses, not for what is not a sin. Maturidi then refutes the Mu'tazila: they claim that sins of those who avoid major sins are forgiven without further action, but he distinguishes between forgiveness (maghfira) and expiation (takfir). Forgiveness means concealing the sin, while expiation means it is removed by a good deed. The Mu'tazila treat minor sins as merely forgiven (concealed), not expiated. Maturidi cites Quranic verses (25:70, 61:10, 2:271) that illustrate good deeds expiating sins. Thus, the Mu'tazila view prevents the proper understanding that good deeds can expiate sins.

Key Terms
مغفرة (forgiveness)
شرك (shirk)
توبة (repentance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Khawarij believed that verse 4:48 implies that all sins except shirk are automatically forgiven without repentance.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the verse distinguishes between shirk and other sins, and does not address the conditions for forgiveness.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is the Khawarij interpretation of verse 4:48 corrupt?
A) Because it implies repentance, which the verse does not permit.
B) Because it denies that shirk is unforgivable.
C) Because it confuses shirk with minor sins.
D) Because it adds a condition that is not in the verse.

Key Takeaway
Verse 4:48 is a categorical distinction between shirk and other sins, not a statement about the need for repentance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verse 4:48, do you automatically assume that your other sins are forgiven because you believe in tawheed? How does Maturidi's distinction challenge that assumption? What must you actually do about your sins?
?
The Khawarij used this verse to justify extreme positions. Have you ever taken a single verse out of context to support a comfortable belief about your own salvation? How can you guard against that?
?
Maturidi says the verse 'does not permit the implication of repentance.' Have you ever assumed that simply knowing the truth (tawheed) is enough without active repentance? What sin have you not repented from today?

Refuting Khawarij on Verse 4:31 and Expiation
Maturidi refutes Khawarij and Mu'tazila on verse 4:31 and expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of Khawarij and Mu'tazila interpretations of verse 4:31 and the concept of expiation (takfir) for minor sins.

Core Idea
Expiation (takfir) removes minor sins through good deeds, not just forgiveness.

Imam Maturidi continues to refute the Khawarij and Mu'tazila by examining verse 4:31 ('If you avoid the major sins...'). He explains that this verse mentions expiation (takfir), not just forgiveness, and that the Khawarij and Mu'tazila misinterpret its implications. Let's dive into his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on verse 4:31
Read the Arabic and translation where Maturidi discusses 'If you avoid the major sins...' and the concept of expiation.
Notice how he contrasts forgiveness (maghfira) and expiation (takfir).
2
Understand the refutation of Khawarij
Maturidi says the Khawarij interpretation 'does not permit' because of the expiation mentioned. Why would expiation invalidate their view?
The Khawarij thought avoiding major sins automatically forgives minor sins, but Maturidi argues expiation requires a recompense.
3
Understand the refutation of Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila claimed that sins of those who avoid major sins are forgiven, not expiated. Maturidi says this prevents confirmation of ambiguities and that expiation is real.
Pay attention to the distinction between 'forgiven' (concealed) and 'expiated' (removed by good deed).
4
Connect to supporting verses
Maturidi cites verses like 25:70 to prove that evil deeds are replaced by good deeds through expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قوله : إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ ، تأويل الخوارج فيه من الخطأ فاسد ؛ لأنه ليس بذنب فيغفر ، وفى هذا ذكر المغفرة ، ولا يحتمل إضمار التوبة لما يغفر بمثله الشرك ، والآية فى التمييز بين الذنبين ، وكذلك لا يحتمل قوله : إِن تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ ، ؛ لما فيه التكفير ، وما لا ذنب لا يكفر والخطأ لا يحقق الذنب ، والتكفير يكون لشيء يجز به ، ولا يحتمل ما قالت المعتزلة لأن قولهم يمنع تحقيق الشبه ؛ إذ هي تقع من مجتنب الكبائر [١١٧٦] مغفورة ، وفى هذا اثباتها ، ثم التكفير ، وهم يجعلونها مغفور [٠] لا مكفرة ؛ إذ المغفورة هى التى تستر عليها ، وفى بقائها إلى مدة دفعها ، والمكفره هي التي يأتى من صاحبها فعل حسن يكفر به نحو قوله : " فَأُولَئِكَ يُبَدِّلُ اللهُ سَيِّئَاتِهِم حَسَنَاتٍ ، ٥ ، وقوله : هَلْ أَدُلُّكُمْ عَلَى تِجَارَةٍ ، وقوله : ( إِنْ تُبْدُوا الصَّدَقَاتِ ،
Then His statement: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him' (4:48). The interpretation of the Khawarij regarding it is corrupt error, because it is not a sin that is forgiven. And in this mention of forgiveness, it does not permit the implication of repentance, for that by which shirk is forgiven is similar to it. And the verse distinguishes between the two sins. Likewise, His statement: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden' (4:31) does not permit [their interpretation], because of the expiation (takfir) it contains. And that which is not a sin does not expiate, and error does not confirm sin. Expiation is for something by which one is recompensed. And that which the Mu'tazila said is not permissible, because their statement prevents the confirmation of the ambiguities, since they occur from one who avoids major sins and is forgiven. And in this is affirmation of them, then expiation. They make them forgiven, not expiated. For the forgiven is that which is concealed, and its remaining until the time of its removal. And the expiated is that for which the doer performs a good deed that expiates it, similar to His statement: 'Those, Allah will replace their evil deeds with good deeds' (25:70), and His statement: 'Shall I guide you to a transaction?' (61:10), and His statement: 'If you give alms openly' (2:271).
Source pages p. 936

Commentary
This passage focuses on the interpretation of Quranic verses related to forgiveness and expiation, refuting both the Khawarij and the Mu'tazila. Maturidi first discusses verse 4:48 ('Allah does not forgive shirk'). He says the Khawarij interpretation is corrupt because the verse is about distinguishing between shirk and other sins, not about requiring repentance for forgiveness. The verse mentions forgiveness directly, so implying repentance (tawba) is not permissible here. Similarly, verse 4:31 (avoid major sins) does not require repentance; it speaks of expiation (takfir) of minor sins. Expiation (takfir) is for something that recompenses, not for what is not a sin. Maturidi then refutes the Mu'tazila: they claim that sins of those who avoid major sins are forgiven without further action, but he distinguishes between forgiveness (maghfira) and expiation (takfir). Forgiveness means concealing the sin, while expiation means it is removed by a good deed. The Mu'tazila treat minor sins as merely forgiven (concealed), not expiated. Maturidi cites Quranic verses (25:70, 61:10, 2:271) that illustrate good deeds expiating sins. Thus, the Mu'tazila view prevents the proper understanding that good deeds can expiate sins.

Key Terms
تكفير (expiation)
كبائر (major sins)
شبه (ambiguities)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believed that minor sins are merely forgiven (concealed) without being expiated by good deeds.
Correction: Maturidi shows that expiation (takfir) is a real removal of sin through good deeds, not just concealment.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the difference between forgiveness (maghfira) and expiation (takfir)?
A) Forgiveness is for major sins, expiation for minor.
B) Forgiveness conceals the sin, while expiation removes it through a good deed.
C) Forgiveness requires repentance, expiation does not.
D) They are the same.

Key Takeaway
Expiation (takfir) is a real removal of sin through good deeds, distinct from mere forgiveness which conceals the sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Mu'tazila thought sins are only concealed, not removed. In your own life, do you treat your small sins as if they just disappear, or do you feel the weight of them until you do something to erase them? How does your view affect your repentance?
?
Which of your daily good deeds—like a kind word, a charity, or a prayer—are you consciously offering as expiation for your sins? If none, what is holding you back from making your good deeds deliberate acts of takfir?
